                              Preface

Prelude

       This souvenir is beino published in connection with the
celebration of the Silver Jubilee of our Academy of Compara-
tive Philosophy and      Religion,    founded by the great modern
Saint, Sri    Gurudev    Dr. 8. 0.     Ranade in the vear 1952. It
Consists of 1४४०: volumes < One dealing with Sri Gurudeva’s
Sampradava and Heart-Homages paid to him; and the second
with his Philosophy as well as philosophy and Religion in
general. This first volume has two parts
                                       - The first dealing
with the Pillars of the Sampradaya and the second with Heart-
Homages paid to Sri Gurudev.


Our Academy

       Before presenting the salient features of this      volume,
it would be in the fitness of things to recount in brief, i) the
Aims and Objects of the Academy, ii) its origin and develop-
ment and      iii) its activities,   as the Academy is celebrating
its Silver   Jubilee this year


The Aims and          Objects:

       What does: our Academy stand for ? What are its
Aims and Objects as enjoined. by Sri Gurudev? the Aca-
demy stands primarily for the propagation, of the Spiritual
ideals and the Philosophy of Life of Sri Gurudev. What were
his Spiritual 108812 and Philosophy of Life ? God-realisation
through God-devotion was his Supreme Ideal, which he
practised and preached throughout his life. To him ^“ The one
Spiritual Principle underlying the universe’? was God. So,
one God, one World, one Religion and one Humanity , was the
Ideal which he placed before humanity. “It is only when
humanity comes to recognise this Spiritual Principle’ he de-
clared, ‘‘that there would be harmony and peace among the
different races, nations and creeds in the ४४०110.” And second-
ly, according to him, ‘“‘what        we experience,   what we fee!
and what we realise should alone constitute our Philosophy ,
and it should ‘make our life more divine and therefore worth-
while living.” Moreover, about the function of Philosophy, he
also maintained:        “| have always    believed     that the function
of   Philosophy    is    for consolidation      and   consummation        of
Spiritual Exoerience; and it        is only the acquisition of          this
Spiritual Experience which makes a man worthy of being .the
handiwork   of 500 ? To This end hehas soecifically directed
the Academy, ‘to work for the Spiritual               Unity:
                                                           of.«mankind
and consequent peace and good will upon ६8101 2? and for this
purpose, he enjoined the Academy to bring together                intellec—
tual and spiritually minded persons through Spiritual             Svmpo-
siums,   study and research,      lectures, meetings and: conferences
and philosophical publications.


Origin and Development.

         Our Academy owes its origin to a strong desire of Sri
Gurudev to have such an Institution as wellas to the gift of
thirteen acres of fallow land at Belgaum by H. H. Raj isaheb
of Sangli. And it owes its devalopnant to the untiring self—less
efforts on the part of Sri. J V. Parulekar, a devoted disciple
of Sri Gurudav, who ४४३५ then Deputy Collector at Belgaum.


         Soon after the registration of the gift-deed             in   1952,
Sri Gurudev       created a Public Trust entitled           ^" Academy of
Comoarativa Philosophy and Religion ’’at Belgaum and entrust-
ed the work of its dav3loonent mainty to Sri J. ४. Parulekar.
Many atime he exoressed before him his conviction that
the Academy would in ‘course of tim2, grow into 3 huge
Institution    with     various   activities.   But    as   Sri   Parulekar
was soon transferred fron Balgaum, nothing aporeciable could
be achieved in this respect. It was only when he came to reside
permanently at Belgaum after his retirement. that he could
 wholly devote himself to the work of its development

       Sri Gurudev attained Maha Samadhi in 1957. As he
 was the Sole Trustee and no mention had been,made regarding
 the mode of succession to the trusteaship ;in the application
 for the registration of the Trust.the District Judge of Belgaum,
appointed           a Board of Trustees with Sri G.                    V.    Tulpule,          Ratired
 0.   >. M.    6.       as Chairman
                                 and Sri
                                       J. V. Parulekar, Retired Deputy
Collector       as Hon-Secretzry. The Trust land.                           which was mostly
uneven,       was got levelled and                 was divided into                 several      plots
reserving
        a sufficiently                   large portion for the purpose of con-
structing the present Gurudev Mandir. A                                sizable amount was
realised by sale of plots.                  A portion of it was utilised for
 onstructing the, Stately Building-a                       unique           structure       10    this
part-and        the rest was deposited in Banks,                        which        formed        .the
nucleus       for       starting       the activities       of     the        Academv.            The
construction of Gurudev Mandir was completed in, 1965, and
its inauguration-which was a grand                              function-took place on
8-12-1965           at    the    hands of      the       late    Dr.    S. Radhakrishnan,
the then President of India                                             "|             -

Activities                                                 हा


         With 9 view              to give due publicity to the- Aims and
Objects of the             Academy and create interest among the people
in the    spiritual message               of the. Masters           and       Rational           Mys-
ticism     as expounded by Sri 6८१४०१९५, the Trustees                                decided       ta
carry on the following activities for the present                                                  #


                    `           5 ११                 {|     ८.५५              व            .
Journal


         An Annual Journal entitled ‘' Pathway to God" consists
ing of    learned          articles by’ eminent             scnolars         and seekers on
various important topics concerning Philosophy,                                     Religion and
Culture       was started under the             auspices          of the       Academy. The
first    issue of          the     ध“ Pathway       to    God’’ was             published.         in
November        1966        on‘        Vaikuntha     Chaturdashi              ’’,    the    dayon
which Sri Gurudev received spiritual Initiation. It was continu-
ed as    an    Annual           Journal .for    four       years.      every        issue      being
released      onthe         same ‘‘ Vaikuntha             Chaturdashi           ? day every
year. Since 1970,
                it was made a Bi-annual journal, . the second
issue being             published       onthe’ 6th day            of June,           the date on
which Sri Gurudev attained Maha Samadhi.                                 This arrangement
continued       till October 1976.and                since then, it has. been deve-
loped into a            Quarterly Journal, In            response to the             demand of


                                              11
the subscribars, articles in           Sanskrit, Hindi, Marathi and
‘Kannad   are being published recently in the journal.


Library       —

       A library named * Gurudev Granthalaya * has been
Started by the Academy since 1966. Acollection of about                         one
thousand valuable books belonging to late Sri.                     N: V. Gunaji
was received as donation from his heirs. Some books are being
added to the       library every year       through   donation          as well as
fresh purchase. The Granthalaya contains’ at                     present    about
four thousand books— English, Marathi and Kannada. Reading
facilities are provided to         the members         in    the    Library hall.
Arrangement is also made for issuing books to the subscribers
on payment of       the    requisite deposit    amount.          Many     persons
have been receiving the benefit of these valuable books.


Lectures «


       The Academy has instituted ‘“‘ Gurudev Ranade Memorial
Lectures (series)         in memory of Sri Gurudev. Dr. ए. 0. Ranade.
Every year a distinguished Scholar is invited to deliver a series
of lectures on some         important subject     of    spiritual        interest.
The lectures are delivered        in   Gurudev    Mandir           at   Belgaum.
They are thereafter published in the form of a book on behalf
of the Academy.        There have been up ‘till now eight                       such
series of Lectures-six
                     in English and two in Marathi. Out of
these, five       have been.    already     published       in   the     form     of
books-four
         in English            and one in Marathi. Following              are    the
subjects of these Memorial lectures.

     Nama - Saptaha       `         */                ‘       in


           A Nama - Saptaha is celebrated every year for five days
     in Gurudev Mandir, in    which sadhakas from. different -parts
     of the country, participate. The programme mainly consists of
     Nama-Smarana i 6. Meditationon Divine Name with kakad—
     arati andprayer at Dawn and the Bhajans in the morning,
     afternoon and night. Discourses on spiritual subjects are also
     arranged on 81। the five days.

           Besides al] the Scheduled Activities of the Academy as
     mentioned above, the Academy        has   been       arranging. several
     lectures, discourses and kirtans from time to time throughout
     the year, as and when deserving personalities are available,

     Sri Gurudeva’s ‘Sampradaya

           We shall now try to deal with a few salient features 0
     the present volume. This volume has been divided. into                  two
     parts : The first part
                          is taken up with the account regarding
     the “Pillars of the Sampradaya’’- about their brief Life-sketch-
_    65 as well as about their spiritual ‘message; while the second
    } part contains “Heart - Homages” to Sri Gurudev                  by his
      ‘admirers, students and disciples.

            The Sampradaya of Sri Gurudev is called “ Nimbargi
      Sampradaya `” as Sri Nimbargi Maharaj has been               it’s recent
      Originator in this part of the country. But it even goes back
      to Revansiddha or Revan-Nath as heis also called. Hence it
      appears that Revansiddha assimilated in his teachings the
      Universal aspects of the teachings of both the Nathas and the
      Siddhas. Tradition tells us that he had resided at Renagiri in
      Satara Districtsfor some time and.came down to Siddnagiri
      near Kolhapur,and lived in the jungle there. According to one
      tradition he himself was called “ Kadasiddha’’ as he resided
      in the jungle (kada). According to another tradition his pre-
      mier disciple was 89160 “Kadasiddha”, who established a Math
at Siddha-girj. In the tradition of       this Math    Muppin- Muni or
Muppin-Kadasiddha happens to 88 096 22nd              Pontiff ( Matha-
dhipati) from whom Sri Nimbargi: Maharaj received             Spiritual
nitiation. Such 1510 brief     the     history   of   this Sampradaya.
About this Sampradaya Sri Gurudev had once remarked’: “This
may be called “‘Swarupa-Sampradaya ’’~a Tradition of **          Self-
Vision ”’, which has been adopted since ancient times: by seers
like Narada, Yajnavalkya and others .up to the 7100610 {1168
by saints like Jnaneshwar, Tukaram and Sri Nimbargi Maharaj.


Main     Pillars


         There are five great Pillars in this Sampradaya: viz. i) Sri
Nimbargi Maharaj ii) Sri Bhaussheb M tharuj, iii) Sri Amburao
Maharaj. iv) Smt. Sri Sivalingava and ४) Sri Gurudev Rambhau
Maharaj. They include the originator 85 well as the promoters
of this Sampradaya. They contributed greatly to enhance .and
spread the spiritual glory of the Sampradaya for well-nigh            a
century. They have been catering to the spiritual needs         of   all
the aspirants    irrespective of caste, creed, race or sex. They
have shown them the genuine Pathway              to God, have properly
guided    and   inspired   them and      have    thus enabled them to
attain the Supreme goal of life viz. Divine Vision and Bliss.

         Here we are reminded of a १118 Abhanga by Saint
Bahinabai, the disciple of Saint Tukaram. In it she has
graphically described the “ Pandhari Sampradaya”’ by employ-
ing the metaphor of a temple. ‘‘ The foundation of this
temple. ? she says, “ was laid by Sri Jnaneshwar, 02 which
Sri Namadev constructed a spacious temple; Sri Ekanath
raised a tower over it ( We here take the liberty of introducing
५ tower’? for ^° pillar’? to suit the metaphor well) and Sri
Tukaram placed his beautiful golden spire on the tower. %५

       Likewise. we may make useof this                          in
                                                      fine metaphor
the case of our Sampradaya as well. Sri Nimbargi Maharaj
laida firm broad-based foundation for the temple -of our
Sampradaya, on which his illustrious disciple Sri Bnausaheb

                                 vil
    Maharaj      erected a    magnificent           temple;      Sri    Amburao
    Maharaj and Srimati Sivalingava raised a stately tower over
    it and Sri Gurudev adorned it ‘with his resplendent spire to
    serve as a beacon-light to all the beknighted mariners on the
    turbulént ocean of life


             The relative spiritual greatness and grandeur of. these
    saints    can very well be realised by pointing out parallels
    between them      and some renowned saints of                other parts of
    Bharat. Sri   Gurudev used to say that Sri            Nimbargi       Maharaj
    and Sri Bhausaheb Maharaj had their parallels in Jnaneshwar
    and Tukaram Such was the supreme height of their spiritual
    attainment. Sri    Bhausaheb Maharaj, though a house-holder,
    canbe compared       with Sri    Ramdas, as          there    is a    striking
    resemblance between them in respect of date of birth, teaching
    and organising skill. Sri Amburao Maharaj can bear comparison
    with Sri Kalyan of Sri Ramdas from the point of view of inten-
    sity of sadhana and absolute self-surrender to his Sadguru,
    whom      he regarded    as God incarnate.        Saint Sivalingava has
    her counterpart in saint Muktabai of Jnaneshwar and saint
    Mahadevi Akka of Prabhudev. Sri Gurudev has his parallel in
    Swami        Vivekanand. Just    as    Sri      Vivekanand spread            the
    glory and spiritual      mission of    his       Master   throughout         the
    world. Sri Gurudev, though he differed from Sri Vivekanand in
|    many other respects,     8150 in his own way has tried              to spread
     the glory    and message not only of his Master but also               of his
     Master’s Master as well. Had he been blessed with the robust
     physic of     Swami     Vivekanand        he     would      have    also    like
     Vivekanand     personally carried ‘the spiritual         message       of   his
     Master to allpartsof the world.


     Inspiring Lives


              Now let us try to ascertain soma             important       features
     of the inspiring lives and universal teachings of these saints.

              The first feature that      strikes us     is that       these saints
     belonged to different strata         of     society      and 0        different

                                       Viii
castes,     creeds    and         sex.   They     were        alj     householders.
Financial position of Sri Nimbargi                  Maharaj, Sri Bhausaheb
Maharaj     and     Sri     Gurudev       was _     fairly      well, while       Sri
Amburao Maharaj and Sri Sivalingava                     had at        times to face
the   penury      of the worst type. Excepting                  Sri    Gurudev all
others were not educated in               the modern sense of the word.
Naturally their literature is meagre, though spiritually very
valuable and inspiring, as it is an outcome of their rich Spiri-
tual Experiences. Sri Sivalingava, however,was endowed with,
high poetic genius. The poems and songs which she has left
behind “are pulsating with fervent emotion and spiritual
illumination. But         Sri   Gurudev could          have    all    the   facilities
of    modern   education which            he    ably    utilised      for attaining
great intellectual eminence. At the same time he had also the
good    fortune of experiencing supreme spiritual illumination
through the unbounded grace of his Master. Hence. the legacy
of his philosophic and            spiritual    literature      is simply unique,
instructive as wellas           illuminating.     It throws a flood of          light
on the cryptic teachings of his great Masters as well as on
those of eminent ancient sages and saints of Bharat. He could,
hence, clearly expound their message to the modern scientific
minds in a thoroughly rational manner.


          These    saints       have     received      initiation       from their
respective Masters at different stages of life. There is also
a good deal of disparity in the nature of their conversion.
Excepting Sri Amburao Maharaj in whom conversion took
place     suddenly        after    initiation,    the conversion            in other
saints took place gradually as they carried on their sadhana
with varying degrees of intensity and regularity. However,
after conversion, the intensity gradually developed in all of
them, as they had tha good fortune of having good spiritual
experiences through the grace of their Masters. These spiritual
experiences in their turn Intensified their faith and meditation
still further, which granted them higher and higher blissful
spiritual experiences. Thus their spiritual evolution went on
developing till they all attained the acme of Self-realisation
and gained the authority of initiating other aspirants.

                                          ix
         Even suffering had       its       share   10     intensifying     their
sadhana. Jealousy, bereavement and acute illness proved to be
blessings in disguise. They        all endured them with fortitude
and equanimity and did not              allow       them    to disturb their
Sadhana. They were all placed in             retatively adverse          circum-—
stances. But they could stillrise above them with the aid of
their Master’s grace. This shows that a strong will and                     firm
faith,    coupled   with   profound devotion,             would      enable     an
aspirant to overcome mountains of             difficulties and attain          the
cherished Ideal.

          In   this connection    the       Life-sketch of         Sri   Gurudev
deserves soecial mention, The five glimpses of his Ideal Life
would serve as fine modals for the                  youth    to    imitate and
emulate. They clearly point out how Sri Gurudev became                         an
Ideal Student-Aspirant,      an    Ideal      Professor-Seeker, an          Ideal
Philosopher-Saint an [deal        Master-Apostle,           and finally how
he developed
        a Unique            Personality on           account       of which    he
०००10 deliver a Universal Messags to humanity.


          Another special feature worth noting in                 their lives is
that they had brought about a           hirnonious         synthesis betwetn
their worldly life and spiritual life.         They did not regard total
renunciation of       worldly    life as       absolutely      necessary       for
spiritual life. On    the other hand, they treat worldly life                   as
complimentary to spiritual life and they led their worldly                     1.16
in such a way as to facilitate their Spiritual Sadhana.

          One more special feature of this Sampradaya is that
these saints never indulged in performing                miracles.       However,
 God      at   times performed    miracles to spread              His devotion
 through       them; but the saints were not even                  aware about
 thein.

          In this way the Inspiring Lives of these great saints will
 not fail to remind and convince us that like them we can                     also
 make our lives sublime provided we earnestly strive for it.


 Thair Universal Teaching

           The metaphysical,     ethical and         mystical       teaching    of

                                        x
these saints is universal, rational and practical. It is mainly
based on their personal experience-both worldly and spiritual.
They never indulged in mere theoretical speculation. They
mainly recognised two aspects of one Spiritual Entity. The
Spiritual Energy that underlies the entire Universe is one.
They call it, like Upanishadic Seers, ^“ Atman ”’, or Nirguna
Brahman or God, which is ‘‘ Sat, Chit, Anand-’’ Existence,
Consciousness and Bliss and which is also the ”’ Creator,
Preserver and Destroyer.’’ And the second is the saint who
has realised the Atman. They callhim Sadguru or Saguna
Brahman    i. e.   Brahman      with   attributes.    They    regarded
Brahma, Vishnu and Mahesha as the personified powers of the
Atman regarding creation, preservation and destruction of the
world respectively. They also regarded      Rama,Krishna, Narayan
and the like as incarnations of the Atman in the sense of
realised souls and all other minor deities, that are merely
personified forces of Nature, as subordinate to them.


      The Supreme ideal that they advocate is God-realisation
or Self ~ realisation or Self-vision. 1६ consists in the intuitive
apprehension and silent enjoyment of the Bliss of        the Atman.
What is the nature of this Self-vision (Atma-darshana) and
Self-bliss ( Atmanand) ? About Self-vision, the Maitri Upani-
shad says: “ That Luminous Reality, which            comes out of us
in   the ecstatic state of    consciousness   and    appears to our
vision in our own form,        is what we might call the Atman-
The Immortal Fearless Brahman- ( Maitri up Il (2}. And Self-
bliss, according to the Chhandogya Upenishad, consists in the
enjoyn.ent of the supreme happiness by the seeker             when he
has the vision ot the Self ( Atman ) every where.

     Now, what is the spiritual discipline enjoined by them ?
The main spiritual discipline ( Sadhana) is meditation on
Divine Name granted bya realised Sadguru. This Name is
Divinity Itself-God in posse-as it reveals itself to the intu-
itive vision or audition of a Saint at the height of meditation.
Thus, this Name carries with It the Divine Power. Hence
meditation on it becomes a process of identification with
Divinity. Naturally,   it    leads to the   Blissful vision    of the


                                  xi
Atman. But     in order to     achieve this Supreme Ideal,            it is
absolutely necessary for a seeker to strictly practise the moral
discipline which consists in elimination of vices and cultiva-
tion of virtues-especially the central virtue of God-devotion.
Itis only then that he will be able to attain his cherished
ideal of God-redalisation.

        Such is the core of      their teaching, presented           in (i)
 Bodhe-Sudhe of Sri Nimbargi Maharaj, (2) Nama-Yoga of                  Sri
Bhausaheb Maharaj, (3) Practical Philosophy of             Sri    Amburao
 Maharaj, and (4) Elixer for Life as well as Jewels of Thought
of Sri Gurudev. The spiritual thoughts contained in them are
capable of providing necessary light, instruction and              inspira-
tion to all genuine aspirants- -thus proving as a         real   Elixer for
 their life.


 Heart     Homages


      The second part of this volume contains Heart--Homages
to Sri Gurudev. Tney are all expressions of emotional out-
 pourings by his admirers, students        and disciples.        Naturally,
 their emotion has assumed different forms. The admirers have
 expressed their appreciation for the great intellectual eminence
 present in his publications and lectures as wail as his warmth,
 sincerity and   simplicity,   displayed in      his behaviour        with
 all those with whom he came in          contact--The      students    are
 all full of gratitude to him as he was a friend, philosopher and
 guide to them all. Sri   Gurudev        had   rendered     loving    help
 10 many 3 poor deserving student in all possible ways in             their
 higher education. He even treated them as inmates of his own
, household.   Hence they have gratefully expressed their pro-
। found Jove and respectful admiration tor his generous affection
 showered on them The emotion of his disciples has assumed
 the form of reverential devotion. To them Sri             Gurudev was
 Divinity itself in flesh and blood.           Hence   their devotional
 fervour for his spiritual grandeur and guidance                 has found
  expression in fheir devout homages.

                   Sri   Nimbargi                  Maharaj
                             (1790-1888 )

                                        (1)
                   A BRIEF LIFE - SKETCH
                         ( M. ७. Deshpande )

   Sri Narayanrao Bhausaheb-popularly known as Sri Nimbargi
Maharaj, can very well be        regarded as a            Spiritual Bhag7rath.
Just as King Bhagirath had, by his                  intense,   penance brought
down the Heavenly Ganga, to the parched earth and                       enabled
it to bloom with fresh verdure, our Spiritual                    Bhagirath     also
had.    by   his   intense    meditation,            brought   up the Spiritual
Ganga, that had gone underground for centuries in this part
and enabled the pining        hearts to enjoy her blissful            ambrosia.
This holy Divine Stream, originated and issued from his heart,
gradually gained      momentum          and         expanse    from   his    great
disciples and aspired to reach the ocean of humanity through
Sri Gurudev. Hence Sri Nimbargi Maharaj has been                       regarded
as the originator of this Sampradiya.

       Sri Narayanrao        belonged         to     8   Virasaiya    family     of
Nimbargi. a village in the Indi Taluka of Karnatak. When he
was a youth of 25, once he was severely scolded by his father,
for taking active part in the Holi                 revelry. In a fit of burning
remorse and shame, he repaired to Pandharpur and                        ardently
prayed the Lord for three days, to pardon                  him    for his    folly
and guide him by the right path.                   On the third day. the Lord
Nimbargi Maharaj



Vithal appeared in his dream and assured him:                      ‘‘ Child, don’t
worry ! Go to Siddhagiri. You wiil find your                   Master to guide
४०७.” Thts assurance restored his balance and he returned home
in a normal mood.A few days afterwards, he went to Siddha-
giri, near Kolhapur, on a           pilgrimage. It was the place of his
family God - Sri Kadasiddhesvara. After finishing the worship
of Siddhesvara, he began to search               his    Guru.      He     had    just
come out of the Temple, when he saw a Yogi, 8                    emerging out
of a cave nearby and beckoning               Narayan        to approach him.
Greatly attracted by the            lustrous     figure, Narayan           literally
rushed towards the Yogi and fell athis feet. The Yogi gently
raised him and took him inside his cave     There he blessed
 him with the Divine Nama,           and advised         him      to meditate       on
it regularly. “ff you         do    this   sincerely ? he said ‘‘your fame
would spread in all quarters.’’Fully satisfied with this blessing
of the Yogi, Narayan returned home. But soon he was absorb-
 ed in his family     life     and    didnot       attend         to    meditation
 properly, for   about six years.          Realising this          negligence       on
 the part of   his chosen disciple, the Yogi one day came to the
 house of Narayan. Greatly surprised by the sudden                       arrival    of
 his Guru, Narayan respectfully welcomed him and worshipped
 him     He    paid 75. 2/.    as     Gurudaksana to the               Guru,     who
 graciously returned them back and advised him to use one for
 the Prapancha and       the second for hi Paramartha. He solemnly
 Promised his     Guru    that       he    would       attend     to   meditation
 without fail, in future.          Overwhelmed with             emotion     he      fay
\, Prostrate at the feet of his Master. And before                 he could        rise
¦ भात express his humble gratitude to him,                  the   Yogi    suddenly
 left him.


       This incident brought about           4   revolutionary          change  in
  the outlook of Narayan. He made a firm resolve to                       meditate
 regularly with one-pointed devotion.                  He    gaveup        his     pro-
  fession of dyeing      and adopted the occupation of a shepherd
  as that was very helpful for his meditation. He daily                     used to
  take his flock along with the flocks of other boys,request them
                                                                             -‘Life-Sketch



to look after his flock and spend               the       whole       day      10       soulful
meditation under the shade of a                 tree nearby. Thus did proceed
his    continuous Sédhana, day                after day, month after                 month.
and year after year. without the help and guidance of anybody.
He received guidance and inspiration from the 11/71                                     resid-
ing in his heart. for his spiritual progress.                    He     thus      went      on
Progressing       from     stage to. stage for well-nigh                   36 years.        He
visualised the -I/man, conversed with the Arman,                            played with
the Arman and ultimately merged in the Infinity of the Atman,
and enjoyed the ecstatic Bliss. He thus reached the                                 pinnacle
of spiritual elevation.


        The external life of         Sri Narayanrao Maharaj                   was        quite
uneventful. But his inner spiritual life must have been                              replete
with     thrilling       incidents     But as it was 8 sealed book, none
could know its grandeur. Sri              Maharaj          never      revealed           it to
anybody. A few experiences only                  that casually slipped                   from
his reluctant lips and picked up by his most                       beloved          disciple
Sri Bhausaheb Maharaj, have               become known                to    us.     We     are
told that Sri     Maharaj        Visualised the fullform of                  the     (काका
from tip to toe, he had the vision               of      Pancavadana - the               Lord
with five faces,as weil as of Brahma, Visnu,and Siva, one above
the other. He had also experienced the vision                         of     the Infinite
-of Nirbayalu.       He    had    heard       and        visualised supersensuous
Divine Nimas and hence he was supposed to have brought                                     the
Nama from Heaven.

        After attaining the highest spiritual goal, he                            lead     the
blessed life of a Jivanmukta - a Liberated Saint. He entrusted
the   management of the           houschold           affairs      to       his     son and
devoted his entire life exclusively                 to    Paramartha. He carried
on his Sadhana,           blessed the deserving              aspirants.           and    gave
discourses on Dasbodha.This went on for 28 years. After leading
fsuch
    a perfectly fruitful.            blissful    life.     Sri    Maharaj attained
Samadhi at the ripe age of 95,                in1885, leaving              behind him a
few valuable songs and [८५८८7705 for the benefit
                                               of the aspirants.
as    wel.   as   a great Sampradiya                of    Rational          Mystics        for
spiritual    welfare      of humanity.


                                          3
Nimba:gi Maharaj



      51 Maharaj thus belonged to the galaxy of the greatest
of men, who lived and passed away unknown and whose thou-
ghts later on, found expression in the second   rate heroes who
became known to the world.         “ He was.’ in the     words of
Sri Gurudev, ^“ like a Bakula tree,   whose flowers.    though       in
acorner, would send their fragrance, throughout         the    length
and breadth of Karnatak.”

       jangama was the appelation which Sri Maharaj    has    used   as
       his Mudrika in his songs,
              2

    BODHA-SUDHE.

  (Words of Eternal Wisdom)

         `   OM
        न Prayer.


             (1)
O Master of Masters mine !
    Mysterious Thy might Divine.
May not my mind ever feel
    Attracted for the worldly weal.
Full well my devotion swell
    And ever in Thee my mind may dwell.
May God display His splendour
    Before my eyes of wonder.


             (2)
Plant in me Thy righteous seed
    Supplanting all the wicked weed.
May my mortal coil
   Always in Thy service toil.
May my thoughts ever glow
    And words resplendent from me flow.
May my deeds ever shine
    In Thy brilliant Light Divine


              5
Nimbergi Maharaj



                              (3)
                   May my mind forever
                       Thy hallowed Name remember.
                   Nor pine for other things
                       That never lie within its wings.
                   May it drink the nectar full
                       That springs from Thy Name withal
                   May it plunge like a fish
                       In the ocean of Thy Bliss


                               (4)
                   Thy Grace shall be the food for me
                       Thy Grace shall be my drink.
                   Thy Grace my vital breath shall be
                       From no terror shall! shrink.
                   May the fountain of Thy love spring up
                       And pour a nectar-shower
                   Eternally to bring me up
                       That I may fully flower.


                                (5)
                    Thy measured words like lightening bright
                    Lend my heart Thy light and might.
                    May Thy voice like thunder fall
                    And drive my penury once for all.
                     INTRODUCTION

                     (77, 6. Jamkhandi )



      1]   Sri   Narayanrao   Maharaja     of   Nimbargi   was
the spiritual Paramaguru of Sri. Gurudev Dr. Ranade, being
the spiritual preceptor of Sri. Bhausaheb Maharaj, who
initiated Dr. Ranade in the mystical path. Readers of the
‘Pathway’ may remember that translations from the sayings of
Sri Nimbargi Maharaj entitled‘‘Bodha-Sudhe’’ or ‘‘Words of
Eternal wisdom 18९6 been given, from time to time. [१ is in
the fitness of things that we pay our tribute of respectful
homage to the memory of the great Saint by giving a_ brief
outline of his teachings.

      2]   It is very difficult to write about great men whose
outlook and experiences are far, far different from those of
ordinary men and one has to be very careful to     see that no
injustice is done to their memory. The spiritual tradition
inherited by Sri. Nimbargi Maharaj and bequeathed by him
has been continued, after his passing away, by Sri Bhausaheb
Maharaj.Sri. Amburao Maharaj and Dr. Ranade. The writings

                               7
 Nimbarg: Mahazej



 of Dr. Ranade hims2lf provice an authentic exposition                          of
 the essential ideas of      this spiritual heritage.           It is the same
 ancient, spiritual pathway, which has been hallowed by the
 great saints of India, from the earliest times. It is the path of
 devotion, consisting of constant            meditation     on the       Divine
 Sabija-Nima-—Divya-Néma ieceived by                the disciple         from    a
 spiritual     preceptor who     has attained       God-realization.        The
 spiritual progress of the disciple ९606005 on the observance of
  rigorous morality. The path is through            and through      rational.
  from the initial approach, to the ultimate            consummation            in
  Self-realization, God-vision and Ecstatic Bliss.               The goal       of
  human life is spiritual       salvation - the      transcendence         to    a
  higher plane of Divine consciousness.             where there is eternal
  Peace and Bliss.


          3]   It would   be desirable here to eiucidate the various
  elements of this Pathway in some detail and refer to               some       of
\ its broad features. Firstly there is nothing exclusive about it,
 " in the sense that any one, man or woman, of any caste,
  community or religion or race may be initiated and                accepted
  within the fold,     provided he orshe is possessed of           the requi-
  site inner urge for spiritual Sadhana and Salvation. There is no

  distinction of high and low and a sense of spiritual brother-
  hood prevails among all. Sri Nimbargi Maharaj had among
  his disciples persons of all communities


          4]   The next feature is the insistence of            Sri. Nimbargi
  Maharaj      on   purity of    character and
                                            conduct. In  fact,  a
  scrupulous moral life is the very foundation of Spiritual life
  Sri.   Maharaj has stated that one’s conduct             is    one’s    shield
  and if one is pursuing the right          path,   even   God     cannot       do
  him     any harm.     His exhortation is that we should abandon
  all    vices      and cultivate     the    Virtues,     the greatest and
  fundamental virtue being          God-devotion.       It may be recalled
  here that there are various classifications of virtues evolved
  by different moral philosophers but the basic        virtue. in
                                                                    Bodh a-Sudhe



this tradition, is God - Cevotion               and the other virtues neces-
sarily      flow   therefiom. It is       also    plein   that   the   necessary
implication is that whatever comes in the way of                       God-devo-
tion cannot be a virtue.           The morality of a spiritual Sadhaka
is God-oriented and          not    the    usually accepted          egoistic or
social morality. Sri. Nimbargi Maharaj has given very helpful
suggestions for regulating one’s life for realizing the spiritual
ideal       ofman.    He     teaches       us    to   turn   the     search-light
inward and         examine     critically        our conduct       at every step:
Saints are, in a very real sense, great spiritual economists, in
as much as they have realized that the allotted                    span   of life
is the only        capital    for    man and it is, therefore, his main
duty, to utilize every moment for his spiritual salvation and
attain to God vision, in this very life.

        A    famous    Maxim of           a Kannad Saint which is cited
by Sri Maharaj ane which recalls to our mind the                       Sara of
Badarayana Harald: शब्दात्‌- tells us that he who hes been
blessed with the vision             of    an ensign       of God-which also
is God - will never return to Samsara. It is sometimes said
that mystics are on 8 supra-moral plane which only means
that it becomes their nature to act morally and that they are
incapable of acting otherwise. Their actions are God-in-
spired and are performed for God-propitiation, witha sense
of complete surrender               and dedication. Their whole life
becomes God-inspired. God-directed and God-dedicated.

     5] It is not necessary for one to give up the worldly life
altogether for the sake of spiritual pursuit. Infact. all the
great teachers in this line from Sri Nimbargi Maharaj onwards
have been men with a family,carrying on their usual vocations.
The two vows that the disciple is asked to take are the givirg
up of Paradhana and Parastri, avarice and lust, and he is reque-
sted to meditate on the Divine Nama with the utmost concen-
tration. What is needed is a genuine inner urge for renuncia-
tion and not a mere outward show. The essential idea is that
one should develop an attitude of complete Surrender to God.

                                          9
Nimbargi Makgraj



necessarily implying thereby, that it is God who krows what
is beneficial to everyone of us and being omnipotent, would give
us whatever is our due. Our duty is only to meditate on the
Divine Nima and develop a deep and inward devotion for God.
without expecting anything in return. [६ would be noticed
that though one need not give up the worldly life, worldly life
has got to be subordinated to the paramount spiritual pursuit.
Our wor'dly life has got to be regulated and modified, mended
and ended,if necessary, for securing the spiritual End. As Saint
Ekanath says:

         प्रयंच परमार्थ एकरूप होत । आहे ज्यांचा हेत रामनामीं ।।
It is plain that so far as the saint           is concerned.    there is   only
 Paramartha and no            Prapanca,    though for outsiders      it    may
 appear as a combination of both.


     6) It is also necessary to dispel the erroneous              impression
 that prevails in some           quarters that   Mysticism is something
 mysterious and occult and irrational.             It is well   to remember
 that spiritual experiences are quite genuine             and mystics       are
 quite normal          persons who are endowed with normal faculties
 and in some cases            at least, with   extraordinary intelligence
 and penetration, 1 is open to anyone to follow the                 scientific
 method of*‘Hypothesis and Verification”
                                      and there isn                  question
 of any kind of compulsion. It is all 8 voluntary affair and only
 persons with genuine spiritual urge would take to the spiritual
 path and       pursue the same if     they are satisfied       thatthey    are
 getting dividend. There is no scope here for blind faith or sup-
 e:stition. In fact, mystics are real empiricists and they are ina
 position of advantage over the rest,since they have experience
 of both the      »temporal and the spiritual        worlds.     It is a   most
 difficult path, entirely different from purely intellectual disci-
  plines and the prospective Sadhaka has to submit himself to a
  self-imposed code of morality and regulate his life and                  acti-
  vities with a view to further his spiritual progress.He must fully
  realize that the goal before him is not something petty or                tri-
  vial    but     it     15   self-transcendence     and self-realization,—


                                          10
                                                                        Bodha-Sudhe



transcendence of the       lower self and realization                 of the higher
Self-so that, once he reaches                that     stage,   he     is        no   longer
bothered    by the ills of the world. Just as the ills                      of infancy
do not bother an adult, who has out-grown                           his infancy, so
also one who has transcended the                     limited   and    finite         human
existence and has become a part and parcel of the Universal,
Eternal    and   Immortal     Existence,              where     there       is       always
Supreme Ecstatic Bliss, isno             longer bothered             by the          ills of
the world. ‘‘He is in the body but not of 11. We find                                passa-
ges in the Gita and the Upanisads                    which     declare      that once
God is realized. all the shackles of Sumsdra are snenped.. all
doubts vanish and all Karmdas drop away.
The Mundak Upanisad Says :

             भि दश्यते हूदयग्रंथि ः छि द्यन्ते सबंसंशया: ।
             क्षीयन्ते चास्य कर्मा णि        तस्मि    न्‌दृष्टे परावरे ।।

      7]    Another vital feature of this spiritual                   tradition          is
that an integrated-as distinguished from lopsided-develop-
ment is sought after. The individual Sadhaka has full freedom
to regulate his iife and activities with a view to promote and
accelerate his spiritual progress in the light of his own
individual background and         temparament.                 What        is    insisted
upon is the scrupulous observance of the two vows and                                10160-
sive meditation on the Divine Nama. This entails a complete
change of direction in one’s life. The spiritual ideal of Self--
realization-the attainment of the goal at the earliest in this
life itself—ought to 1.11 up and pervade and permeate the entire
consciousness of the Sidhaka and sustained endeavour has
to be made for achieving the supreme end of humanlife. It
is not a matter of practising Sd@dhana, for a few days or
months but the spiritual     efforts have to be persistently
continued to the very last breath. The Gita tells us the same
thing and 50 also reference may be made to the Yogusiitra
of Patanjali (1.14). It is a gradual
                                  but total transformation
of the human consciousness into the Civine Consciousness.
At every step and stage the Sadhaka shou'd feel that there is

                                        11
Nimbargi maharaj




real inward change ard that ke 5 cerryirg all his ectivities
in a better and more efficient manner       ard with the     consci-
ousness that he is doing them for the propitiation of God.


       8]   Sri Nimbargi Maharaj has in his teachings empha-
sized that the only duty of man is to meditate on the Divine
Nama and attain the vision of the Divine.          Susreme       God—
Devotion necessarily implies complete surrender ( आत्मनि वेदन)

This, in 115 turn. presupposes, the purging away of        all    vices
and an exemplary life of      utmost    purity   and   constant    and
00585109 contemplation on the Divine Nama. This is the            supr-
eme goal of all human existence and in the style of the Upanis-

adic teaching उत्ति   ष्ठत, जागृत, प्राप्य वरान्‌ नि वरोधत, Sri. Maha.
raj has also given the clarion call Mods wore च००७००३ ४,०१७

 ae ॥ गुरुचरण कमलदल्ळि      भृंगनागो नी 11 “Do become a bee at the
lotus feet of the Sadguru’’ and     attain Self-realisation.       May
the Lord shower His Blessings on all.


      ‘“‘Bodha-Sudhe”’ is the first Kannada book of Sri Gurudev.
 It is a great-little book-small in size, yet great in    its content.
 He published it in      Devanagari scriot in 1948, “| have lavish-
 ed,” he used to tellus, ‘‘more attention and labour on this
 book than on any other book of 71176." This remark clearly
 indicates the supreme value which he attached to this gem of
 a book.


        We have therefore thought it our duty 10 present           it in
 the English garb for the benefit of a wider circle of aspirants.
  My friend Sri V. 3. Kotabagi-Advocate-Belgaum translated the
 first two parts, while | translated the next two parts, | hope
 that the English rendering that follows would be both interest-
  ing and inspiring to the aspirants.




                                   12
                        (2) Bodha - Sudhe

         # (WORDS OF ETERNAL WISDOM )

                              Part I

        Fundamental Principles of Conduct

1. Blessed human life

    Human life is indeed a rare blessing. It is surely the result
of good conduct in past births, There are four kinds of beings:
those born from the egg or the embryo or those that owe their
existence to perspiration or germination from the earth. The
individual soul ceaselessly wanders through        them.   It passes
through 84,00000 types of lives, perhaps time without number
in one or all of them. It acts waywardly, makes merry,works evil.
suffers immensely and at long last, passes out in utter despair.
Yet, some good somewhere happens to be done to others, and
this unattainable human life is the result. But, if even here:
the life is wasted, in evil deeds, in hankering after the three
possessions of others (viz Woman, Wealth and Lands ), by lett-
ing the six passions loose and the Atman is not realised, this
precious human life is undone. There can be no guarantee of a
return to human existence. We must make the best use of this
human life here and now.

2. The Four Stages and States of life


    All life passes through four stages and states. Childhood.
Youth, Adult-hood and Oldage are the four stages. Ignorance,
Inafatuation. Want and Worry are the four respective states.
      Childhood first: Ignorance then fails to discern the good
from evil and is unable to distinguish what belongs to one-
self and what to others.       Attaining the teen-age. the             ferson
 is struck by a fancy for marriage and mating. That is                  igno-
 rance indeed.


          Youth steps in next. The young man takes a spouse by
 marriage,-that also being the result of good conduct. The man
    and wife love each other dearly. He sets enamoured of his wife
    and acts up to her words. Her words assume greater importance
    than those of his parents. He does not care for         the happiness
    of his parents and makes them miserable. How wicked this ?
    Such scoundrel seldom gets any happiness.


           Attaining the Adult stage, he craves for off-spring. Day
     and night, he pines for them. Meanwhile, as an etfect of
    some good conduct he begets children. Still, without discern-
     ing good from evil, he carries   on   his   sinful    life,    feariessly-
, Then he faces good many miseries.
\




ed         The fourth stage and the last is Oldage.          There the man
     c2aselessly worries as to the fate    of his children          after    him
     and as to how they could be happy in        their    life.    Old age    is
     the hardest lot. An accounting of the sins of his life is              made
     up then. Selfishness and greed are then at      their        height.    The
     sense of mine and thine is prominent. He thus                becomes    the
     butt of ridicule. Deeply involved in worldly life, he forgets his
     own Self (Aiman) and therefore .suffers most. One has. there-
     fore, to remain extremely vigilant during this stage. One should
     Stick up to the Name of God diligently and try to             realise    the
     Atman and free oneself from the Wheel of Existence.

                                                                 Bodha-Sudhe



3.   Strength of Conduct is Strength Divine.


       One’s good conduct is         the only        saviour. One      should
never depend upon      others,    howsoever          slightly.   There is no
other support except     one’s       own    good Conduct. God dwells
within us, holding the scales and metes out justice                 according
to desert.

     All of us hardly ever care for our own conduct and blame
God for the ills   befalling   us.   That     is    unfair. Experience will
teach us that our joys and sorrows            are    but the     result of   our
own actions. It is the    plaintruth        that every one reaps         as he
sows. If we act wisely and wel!, no harm shall ever touch us
even in adream. Conversely. if evil wedo, harm shall ever
pursue us. Remember this: and act wisely and well.

     If one gets somedisease,        that shall have to be          attributed
to one’s own evil doing. Even a prick by thorn can likewise
be had only as an effect of some evil deed. Act well: no disease.
no harm. nor trouble shall befall you.

     The strength of good conduct is unparalleled. Good or evi
follows one’s conduct. Even the Trinity of Gods ( ब्रम्हा, वि ष्णु
महेश) can do no harm-though they so mean - a person possess-
ing good conduct. Then         what       of this    petty human       being !
Conversely, the combined         power of the Trinity Divine fails to
do any good, if one is wanting in ¢ood conduct. That is why
the Saint Purandardas has said:— Se ७२७७ छन
                                          २ ९८० ऊ
८८ | 8६ sedxdsee Bowe “Oh God, if my acts out-
weigh, what can you       possibly do ? ” God            is indeed with us,
if we act well: if we fail in our conduct.            He surely chastises.
Know this fully and always try to act well.

4.   Like seed. Like crop.

     Good or bad is all our own doing. Like seed. like crop. The
seed sown, if bad. the crop too is           likewise bad. Bitter cumin


                                     15
Nimbargi Maharej}



seeds produce bitter cumin weeds; good wheat. produces fine
wheat. Sowing bitter cumin seed, how can you expect fine
wheat for a crop? That is why one must always act prudently
and do good.


      The Cholera Epidemic kills many. Cholera is but a hatchet
 in the hand of God. [१ is He who kills with                     that instrument.
Whatcan the instrument alone do without the wielder ? The
 All-Controller is God,            If, by    good    conduct,        you    816    the
 recipient of His Grace, how                shall   Cholera affect you?           Note
 this; and try to win the grace of God by good conduct.



 5.   As the Sound, so the Echo.


         Others behave with us, as we behave                     with them. Love
 begets love; anger. snobbery and indifference                       are   paid back
 in the same coin. Regard, disregard and fraud also react like-
 wise. Open any account (you choose), the credit znd debit
 entries get    posted       therein accordingly.           You     would     receive
 what you give.            Delight others, you         will      delight    yourself.
 Pain others, you willbe pained yourself. The                       reason is, that
 the Atman is all-pervading. That is how your                       action gets its
 Corresponding        re-action. There            cannot    be     any doubt about
 this.



 6.   Let there be Introspection at every Step


         One should always examine one’s                      conduct      critically.
  Even if a thorn pricks, one           should examine why
                                                   it pricked,
  what fault lay in him and what lapse in conduct was
                                                      respon-
  sible for    it.   All    that    should      instantly     be    ransacked,     the
  mind duly reprimanded and the corduct eccordingly corre
                                                          cted.
  Such introspection, at each step, will always relieve one from
  any contingent harm or disease.

7.   Act up to your Word.

          TA 698 ०७०७९ wD,     Fa
         ‘Conduct consistent with word sets a seal on re-birth”.
‘Nadi’   means good conduct; “Nidi’         means to obey the          words of
your Guru or preceptor. Follow the precepts of the                    sages    and
saints of the past and this very human existence may veritably
be the last.. The individual        self will      be free from rebirth and
shall get merged in the Atman. the Universal Self.

&.   You yourself are God.


         Men in difficulty thus pray to            God;     ‘“‘Oh,   God,    dous
good: Noneelse cando so. You alone                   are competent to do.’’
The true meaning of     this    is    that       ‘‘You     are   your-self     the
Divinity.   As you act, good     or       ill    shall follow        accordingly.
None else can do anything. You                  yourself   do    good.’’      Such
should be the prayer to oneself

               ELIMINATION OF VICES.


9.   Woman Wealth and Property


     All people are caught   up in      the   meshes      of   these    three
(Gunas) objects viz (1) Woman (2) Wealth               and     (3)   Landed
property. God has bestowed upon every one of us these three.
We must be satisfied with      what       has been        granted      to   us
and live contentedly till death.


     We should not day and night be intent u20n others’ posses-
sions and covet them by belittling what we possess or by
treating our own possessions as naught.If we | ००0१९ so at others’
possessions our eyes become corrupt -nay, get accursed ! If we
covet, the mind gets debased and accursed.


      They (the eyes and the mind) are the enemies. If we dance
 to their tunes,   we are undone.
                               We should             never     grant    them
 liberty.


      In case the mind outsteps our control, we should   pray to
 God; but never desire for the possessions of others, The wealth
 and property belonging to others         should    always €           treated
 as forbidden and hellish and we should            rest    satisfied     with
 what God has given us.

                                                         Bodha-Sudhe



10.   Adultery Paves Wav to Dreadjul Hell.

      Even at the cost of death one should be away from adultery.
Adultery causes destruction of wealth, life, body and reputa-
tion, The very life itself is ruined. By this sin one becomes a
destitute in worldly life. Liberation slips out of reach and
dreadful heli is sure to follow.


    Such people are a veritable burden to the earth. They
undeservedly consume food. The earth can never bear their
burden.                ॥

          Good people should therefore look     upon   other   women
as their own mothers. That will give them happiness in world-
ly life    and on surrender to   the     worthy spiritual   preceptor
(Sadguru), they will attain to salvation.

11.    Anger—The Pariah.

      Anger is a Pariah and should always be treated as untou-
chable. Poverty haunts that home where, at all hours, anger
creates restlessness. Nobody likes such people. None will call
them good and every one will condemn them.

      Hence when anger creeps in, it behoves our reason to cast
it away and admonish the mind. Anger should be completely
uprooted.

      It is however excusable to get angry with youngsters with
the object of bringing them onto the right path.            But then.
whatever their mistake may be, the anger should be confined
to oralreprimand, rather than resort to physical force where
there is always a likelihood of a disaster.

 12   Effects of Self-Conceit.

      Man ordinarily is highly conceited. That is indeed very
bad. Conceit pays no dividends.         Many are the faults that flow


                                   19
Nimbargi Maharaj




from it.    It is due to   conceit that pes le arrogantly use            harsh
words to others, nay. even thresh            them.   They       evn   rush   to
assault them and utter all sorts of nonsense.


     Such     men rarely distinguish         between the        small and:   the
great. Conceited      they fail to    understand     how to       speak with
others. Such people even forget their            own     benefactors !       Be-
cause of this conceit they treat floor and dust alike.


     Man will      invariably reap the        fruit of the ills    arising out
of his conceit. He will be paid back in the samecoin by 0111615.
Nobody will even           condescend    to speak with him. He will           be
looked     upon as a worn out shoe. People turn a deaf ear to his
words.


     Remember ! conceit for           anything       is a sure signof         its
coming doom.If man is overproud of his wife,gold or property
or for the matter of that,of his children.wealth, knowledge
strength and other assets,they will disappear or be denied to
 him. A proud king will lose his kingdom, A proud beggar wil!
 go without alms! That is            how God      breaks    our conceit       to
 pieces.


           Similarly we should never be          proud     of    our spiritual
 experiences.
          They will dwindle because of pride. Those willing:
 to lose them may indulge in pride.


           Therefore. when an occasion for such pride offers             itself,
 we should think of those who are far greater               than us and yet
  humble enough and thus correct ourselves.              Knowing this and
  fearing that because of conceit we will lose whatever we have.
  we should nip conceit in bud.If perchance, it crops up, it should
  be driven out. We should enjoy whatever God has kindly best-
  owed upon us and that too without undue publicity.We should
  rest content with that and live happily.

 73.    Jealousy breeds Distress.


       We should never feel sad or jealous at the sight of the
good fortune, high position and progeny of others.       “ The
jealous fellow forfeits his food and pining man, his progeny”’.
            TIBOS.NHOR 59४७ 5 WICMIHTOR ०9२४९,

       Never for a moment think ill of others. If we do so.
misfortune confronts us first, the reason being that the Atman
dwelling in all beings is but one and the same.                      That is       why
we should always wish others            well. Then         God will       bestow
Good Fortune upon us.         consistent with        the    strength          of    our   .
good conduct.


44.     Hypocrisy


         Hypocrisy means outward show of              meditation          on       the
Self (८111100) while inwardly one is engrossed in the thought
of     worldly   objects. We    should       never   entertain         hypocrisy.
because God is omniscient         and    omnipresent.        He knows all.
Therefore never try to deceive Him by means of hypocrisy.


75.     Fraud is       Bad.


        Never defraud others.Fraud is very bad.The very purpose
for which fraud is practised becomes fruitless and is never
fulfilled. Never betray the trust reposed in you by others.
If, through fraud, we obtain the wealth etc. of others, we
lose our own, through fraud. The hand practising fraud gets
polluted.    The seed sown by such hand will               not       sprout        and
no crop will follow.



         We feel glad while misappropriating the wealth of
others. But when the stock of our previous merit is exhausted,
it vanishes in no time and goes off the way it               came.       [t shall
not stay. --       7                     =    3                  #

70.    Snare of Temptations.

        Wife, children. and grand children. involve us in infatu-
ation and that is known as ‘Maya’? (attachment). We                           should

avoid that trap of माह 1. ©. temptations. We should not love
our children too much. At the same time, we must not fail to
arrange for their food andclothing.          We      should         behave with
them as though they are the children of              others.        If we bestow
extra care on them out or selfishness,               it    will        harm    them.
Going the way they do.        we should not involve ourselves into
the trap of their    Méayd-attachment and                0800018       pariners   in
their joys or sorrows.

        It is this infatuation that entraps us. Trapped thus we
are rolled about.    We have therefore to fight against                       it and
become free from      its   fetters.    On     its       approach, we should
 remonstrate our mind and cut off            the     roots     of      infatuation.
 This, indeed, is the real daily sacrifice. Sacrificing of all our
 vices thus, is tantamount to securing great merit.


 17.    Disasters of Injustice.

          It sometime appears that an act            of     injustice becomes
 beneficial and an act of justice        causes           greatloss.          Evenon
 occasions like this justice should           ‘never      be     let    down.     We
 should never misbehave. The loss occasioned by this is visible.
 If our    conduct   is   straightforward          all    that      loss   will   be
 reimbursed by the Inner Witness,God Arman). On the other hand
 if our conduct be faulty and injustice occurs,we cannot possibly
 bear the invisible loss e. g. the loss of wife in                the      prime of
 life or the loss of children during oldage.              We should therefore
 advise our mind thus:      «the visible loss        is    bearable:       but    the
  invisible loss is indeed too difficult to bear. How can others
  harmus? Despite good conduct,          if    loss       is   occasioned.        we
  should consider that some impending danger is past. We can
  bear the harm done to us by others. But we cannot withstand
  the punishment inflicted upon us by the Afman.”

                                                               Bodha-Sudhoe



 18.    Proper Punishment for Sin.


          So far as we understand. we should            stay    away    from
 sin.    We should desist from it. Sins        unwittingly
                                                  done bring
 about some unwitting loss; conscious sin is duly punished.


        To illustrate - suppose we steal a cucumber from some                  -
 field, the husbandman, on seeing it, may scold or perhaps
 beat us.     But for   house-breaking or murder, we           are scolded.
 beaten and handcuffed or are even sentenced to               imprisonment
for life.


 19     The Three Modes of Punishment


          Immoral conduct entails three        types     of    punishments
viz. the physical. the spiritual and the divine.


          Physical punishment consequent upon our sins             denotes
beating by others, punishment by state, harm by bird or beast
or wrath of elements inflicting pain or suffering to the body.
Thus punishment dealt by others is characterised as physical.


          Spiritual punishment constitutes the agony to the soul.
Disease or pain afflicts the body        and     mind    and    makes one
grieve.

          The Divine punishment is that whichis in store              for us
 after death. to be inflicted by Yama. the God of Death.

          Considering    these   three   types   of     punishment,     we
should desist from sin.


20.     Shun Secrecy


       Never act secretly in the affairs of life. We ought to
behave unafraid of others. We might however resort to secrecy
regarding our own domestic acts. For that, we need not he

Nimbargi pblaharaj



afraid of others.    The    Spiritual     Sadhana         alone     should       be
practised in secrecy.      Barring   this, nothing          else    should       be
secret.



 21.   Idleness—the Arch-Enemy.


          We should never     remain 1016.      tdleness      ruins not only
 the idle person but also his whole family.               It is the characte-
 ristic of idleness to ruin    those      who      give     scope to      it.    We
 should,     therefore. remain far away from it.


          Idleness is equally harmful to        spiritual      life. When we
 are occupied in meditation sleep creeps              in     and    idleness       is
 stabilised. We should drive off that sleep when it comes in
 and persist in meditation.  ॥ we ५0 52 for a fortnight or so.
 it departs. The work which  idleness              prompts         us    to     defer
 should instantly be completed.

          If we carry on in this manner, it becomes a habit                     with
 us. To start with we have to 08 brave.             After a time. idleness
 will vanish.


 22.      Crop of Worry.


           Anxiety or worry is exceedingly bad.              its    crop grows
 very rapidly. Hence the moment it 20268175 it should be nipped
  in the bud. Advisethe       mind      and     uproot       worry. Worry          is
 oldage and contentment is youthfulness.


           Men go on worrying right from birth to death. As they
  go on worrying     it simply -grows.        But    their     worrying         does
  not solve the problem. It is the        God’s      will    that       ultimately
  prevails and these people only tire themselves by worrying.


           We should first be careful enough about our belongings
  50 as not to lose them. But when            we    1056,     we    should        not
  worry about the loss. We should not cry over spilt milk. May
  be some impending danger is avoided thereby. Perhaps 3

23.       The Aspiration for the Absolute


           Spiritual aspirants should     not    worry      about     worldly
matters; but they      should   be    ardently    intent.     upon    having
greater and greater vision of the Arman          and 8150 on        acquiring
1.16 ambrosial juice of God’s        name. This means that he should
always be thinking of the Absolute (1101401). If they meditate
always on the Atman, He in turn looks up to their well-being.
He willcater to their      needs   and    keep    them        above     want
throughout their life.


          The sole remedy to destroy the very seed of anxiety and
clean up the mind of all dross is the Divine Name received from
the gracious      (Sadguru) spiritual teacher.Meditation on God’s
name uproots all      ar.xiety and God showers His            mercy on the
spiritual aspirant.                                 :

               CULTIVATION OF VIRTUES


24.   Discrimination   (Viveka)


       Discrimination is the only supreme weapon to fight the
vices. Nothing should be done without discrimination. One
should become vigilant by seeing others stumble and fall. One
should act with foresight in doing everything and should van-
quish all enemies (vices) with the help of contentment and
meditation on the SELF (4tman).

25.   Prudence.


       Our Buddhi (Reason) may save orkill             us. Right     reason
saves us and the wrong one        kills. It   is the    rightly directed
reason which      leads   to ceaseless meditation         on   the    SELF
(Atman). \t is otherwise if it makes one turn away from the
Self and leads one to worry about one’s affairs.Possession of
wealth etc. will be of no avail when crisis comes, but it is the

 rightly-directed reason which would save us. Therefore. one
 should constantly pray to GOD (Arman) to give
                                               rightly direct-
 ed Buddhi (Reason).

                                                          Bodha-Sudhe



26.   Restraint of Senses

       There are ten senses. five sensory or cognitive and five
motor or active.   One should exercise strict contro! over one’s
senses, should not    yield   to   their   demands, but    successfully
resist and   subjugate them. They would         come fully under our
control only when they are all wholly employed in the service
of the ‘Self? (4tman).

       It is only he who has thus conquered and sublimated the
senses that is a real Hero. a real saint and a God Realiser. He
has achieved fulfilment of the mission of human           life. The only
purpose of human life is to achieve this supreme fulfilment.

27.   Destroy Desires First


       Man is swayed by six innate passions,(Vikdras),Desire,
Anger, Arrogance, Jealosy, Hypocrisy,          and Pride. These      are
responsible for the ceaselessly recurring       cycle of Births and
Deaths.


       They should not be permitted to run a riot. Hence.
Desire itself should be eliminated first. One should always
suppress desire by advising one’s mind, “५४1५ should | want
anything? | do not want anything”. There would be thus no
scope for anger to rise. Desire when frustrated, leads to anger.
In the absence of desire. the very foundation of anger would
be absent. Where there is neither desire. nor anger, the rest,
having no foothold, do not arise at all.

       Even if desire springs up inthe mind, the body ought to
be restrained, and should not be allowed to follow the dictates
of the mind.    '“मन गया तो जाने दो          । मत्‌जाने दो Ta”
‘Though the mind goes astray,           let not the body follow,”
Says a Hindi saint.


       The mind has got to         be regulated and controlled by
constant meditation(Sa@dhana). 11 it refuses to give up passions

Nimbargi Mah     raj




it should be advised by Reason; and with the help of                     regular
meditation, constant watch should           be    kept   on   the passions
( {1८61745 ). The       best   man should be without      any       ( Vikdras )
pessions because any ९85118 at the moment                of   death        would
entail another Birtn.


28.     Donot be a Burden


         One should not be burdensome to any one                Any burden
so imposed on others, would undoubtedly recoil                 in    the same
way 6. 9. if formaintenince,maintenance would be burdensome
to oneself.     if   for bodily services. one’s        body     itself     would
become unbearable.


 29.    Donot hold down your hand (like a beggar).

         One should never lower one’s hand for one’s                 needs.     If
 one takes thus from others,one’s wants would ever remain unsa-
 tisfied. The begging hand would be cursed and polluted. There-
 fore,one should always have one’s hand raised up(for giving).


         Priests and Jangams get their hands cursed                   by their
 greed for other’s property and by lowering their hands for that
 purpose. They will therefore never succeed in their undertakings:
 their poverty         willnot cease and their wants would                 remain
 unsatisfied.        Therefore,   one should     not   accept       from    others
 anything gratis or in charity. One should be giving                 to    others
 within one’s means.


  30.    Tolerance


          One's action should always be above reproach from any
  one. If one is unjustly reproached or even beaten,                one should
  not retaliate and one’s love for them should not be diminished.
  Those who do wrong. verily consume poison. Tney will                      suffer
  and dia of the poison. Since they have acted wrongly. God
  will surely punish them in some way

                                       28
                                                             Bodha-Sudhe



         One should bear rebukes from superiors or those in autho-
rity and should quietly tolerate        rebuke-unjustified-even       from
inferiors.    Generally, others willrebuke if one commits mistakes
and one should feel that       rebuke is for his good and should          be
grateful to them. Those,who      sincerely advise with rebuke, are his
benefactors:     those who advise with an apparent smile are his
ill-wishers.‘‘The more the tolerance, the greater        the success in

life’. (“ 2०८2) Save, EN; ४२९६१.) This is so, because tolerance
gives immediate results. viz. peace and happiness. One cannot
be   happy without inner peace. One          endowed with tolerance
will prosper in life.   Penance is the    art   of facing the buffets of
life with due tolerance. One must quietly bear a!| suffering.Inner
contentment should never be allowed to be ruffled.            One should
be   a     veritable ocean    of contentment.     A   real   Saint   is   he
who is evercontented.It is beneficial to oneself to bear with pa-
tience the burdens of others.A little tolerance would avert many
impending disasters.Hence,it is better to do such a            profitable
business.Making a little sacrifice in price,one obtains infinitely
more in spiritual measure from          Arman. Tolerance is the price.
and what is bought is the bliss of the Atman.

3!       Donot give offence
    No offence should be given to another in‘any way, nor
should anybody be annoyed, nor displeased, nor harassed, nor
should be made to feel humiliated. The expectations (hopes)
of others should not be frustrated.

     One should not cause ५1511655 to anyone in any way:
One should not       therefore persist ina bargain and seek to
enforce it, if it causes loss to another. It should be abandoned
with a view to render him happy. If one engages coolies for
work they should not be deceived by short payment. If one
wants to build a house, no wrong should be done to any one.
There should 9610 encroachment nor unlawful grabbing of
timber etc. All things should be willingly bought. ॥ injury
and loss are caused to others in its construction. one would
suffer the same fate so long as he resides in it. If others are
made happy, one would have happiness in return.

32-      Truth-un-truth


       One should always speak the truth and should never utter
 a fatsehood, so that one’s speech would never be futile. If one
 goes on speaking the truth, whatever heutters would prove
 true.       if    cne speaks   untruth whatever one uticrs wouid prove
 f alse.


         One should never stoop to falsehood. even if being truthful
     would        lead to trouble. It is self-deception            to   think that by
     falsehood one could escape             trouble. On theother hand,                one
     would have to face greater troub'e thereby                    Risk or no risk        to
     oneself, one should never utter falsehood.



           Even      if   adherence   to   truth    were      to result      in   loss    of
      money and property etc.,             let   them go.
                                            Our Gracious God is
     omnipotent and not a pauper. Only what hegives would satisf
                                                                 y
     and endure. How much could men give ? One's motto should be
     “death is far better than             untruth ``. One’s creed Ought to be
     ‘no falsehood even at the cost of one’s own                           fife. God will.
      indeed. help such a man in his work.


           This inexorable rule is subject to onty one exception, viz one
     may utter a falsehood even            at    one’s       own   risk.    for securing
     benefit to others e.g. to save some one’s life.


           There is an old story in this connection.


           Kabir Mahiraj hadseen                a Brahmin beating           his wife to
     death.       Therefore,   he was called as          a   witness       to prove      the
     beating. Kabir Maharaj realised that                the Brahmin would
                                                                   1056
     his life tf he spoke the truth, and if he did not, it would cast 8
     blot on his character as a saint. He went to court meditating
     on the SELF (tman , and began to turn his face wherever he
     saw the Self (Atman). He was asked to stand Properly and to
     depose to what he saw.           Kabir Mahérja said * The seer (eye)
