                                (27)
                  God’s Grace Saved            India


        Next day the conversation began with a question by
 Prof. A. regarding the then political situation of India (1944).
 Sri Gurudey remarked : ** The burning power of        war, has now
 grown 50 fierce that it is no use talking of      independence at
  such atime. Even though we somehow got independence, the
“big powers surrounding our country, that are hourly waiting to
 ‘pounce upon us, will easily snatch our independence in no
 time. Our people fly away helter-skelter, when asingle bomb

                                 - 247
                                                                 Elixir for Life



explodes somewhere. They are so panicky. They are not                      able
to protect themseives in any way.             In this    respect no     nation
in the world is so helpless as India.”


      Recently Japan would have created terrible havoc here,
in the twinkling of an eye. But the grace of the Saints in our
country, saved us as we are destined to play a prominent part
in bringing about peace in the world, after this war                  is over.
It is because          ‘Do Little” flew from China and bombed Tokio
that the calamity mentioned            above was averted. Thus really
‘Do-Little’ proved          himself to be ‘Do Great.’ The Almighty
prompted him to take that step and saved                India.   God’s ways
are, indeed, unfathomable. We            cannot    divine the means by
which He achieves His object. We              know how, as the story
goes, God saved the bird, both from the hunter as well as
from the hawk. He made a snake bite the hunter, as a result
of which        his    arrow missed    the   aim   and killed the hawk,
instead. The hunter also died of snakebite. And thus the bird
was saved. If Do Little had not bombed Tokio India would have
been reduced to ashes by the Japanese bombers. A nation that
sent the invincible warships like ‘Prince of Wales’ and
‘Repulse ? to the bottom of the ocean within a short time,
would have easily showered a rain of fire, over India and
burnt it in no time.


      You should seek independence when you deserve it.
What is the testimony of history? We are quarelling with our
own people like hogs and dogs. Under these circumstances,
we should lay the foundation           of physical glory coming           out
of spiritual glory. 1 am stating this ‘merely with the help of
historical logic. | cannot say when such a time would
come. The logic of history requires us to fulfil one of ` these
‘conditions before:
                 we can deserve independence.


           i)     The quarrel between Hindus and Muslims must be
                      ended somehow.


                                      248
Rambhawu Mahara}



          ii)     We must achieve scientific development superior
                 + toboth America and Germany, which is rather
                  impossible.


          iii)    We must rise to such a spiritual    height that we
                  must realise that all humanity     is one.


      It. is the fond belief of some people that we can ४१
independence with the halp of Russia. That is impossible.
Russia is a great—. He has evil designs on             India.   In fact.
every strong nation has such
                           a design. Russian affection is
like that of boa. We cannot say            when he would devour us.

                            My Philosophy


      Once Sri Gurudeo was asked to explain the nature of
his Philosophy when he said : ‘‘ How । live is my Phi!osophy.
1 am a Sthitaprajna in God-realisation and not in behaviour.
My spiritual experience has granted me a firm cenviction
regarding the existence of God. | am perfectly convinced
that God alone is real and everything else - body, creation
etc- is unreal. We may define Sthituprajna as one who is
firmly fixed in his spiritual experience. But my spiritual
experience has not directly influenced my conduct. My anger
is still there, even though very often it                is   an     outcome of my
physical weakness. Peace is only an                  outer expression of inner
experience.       It   does     not   mitter    even     if     it   is    not    always
 present.    It is          the experience that       matters.            We do come
 across people with no spirituality, enjoying peace                              But we

 of ettort   and       is    imprinted    in my      intellect       by    my    spiritua

vision. * When desire departs, God would reside in the heart ”
says   Tukaram.



      That which grants us vision of God is our Religion and
our Ethics. But Kant thinks otherwise: “I may attain God
or | may not. | shall perform my duty.” His Categorical |
Imperative is of that nature. [t enjoins the performance of
duty for the sake of         duty.


     It is idle to say: « | shall attend to devotional practice
in my old age.” Because, “ [ऽ life at your command?” asked

                                     (40)
      Nature of Nama and Internal Meditation


        “ How to carry on             internal     meditation on               Nama?”
was the question,         asked      by Dr. K.       one evening              when Sri
Gurudeva explained : “ There               is no     End other than             Nama”
 is the opinion held by some while others opine: there is
no    Means other       than    Nama.”        Both        opinions        are equally
valid. Nama is both the              End as well      as     the     Means. Nama
 shows the Ripa( Form) of God.                     Hence      it    is    a    means to
 the seeker. But to those who are out, exclusively to meditate
 on   Nama without caring            for    the    vision    of     God,       it   is    an
 End in     itself.


           Sri Tatyasaheb Ranade             got himself           initiated by Sri
 Maharaj and in 1904 at 4 P. M. he saw the spire of the temple
 at Incagiri studded with           spiritual     pearls. Thereafter, without
 Caring for spiritual experiences, he carried on his meditation
 as   asacred duty till his death.            To him Nama was an End in
 itself.

           Meditation     should be        sincere    and     soulful.          Nama is
  a symbol forrealising         the    Ultimate       Reality       underlying            the
  Universe.    ‘ @ iti ekaksarath brahma’’- Om is                    the       Absolute.
  We should undersiand the significance of this        Mantra. Mere
  vocal utterance of Nama             becomes mechanical. We should
  properly understand          the    relation       of     Ripa-Form,              Bhava-
  Devotion      and   Nama-Name.           Form is Mystical          entity or Spi-
  ritual entity;      Devotion is a        Psychological           entity or         Moral
  entity; while        Name    is    Mysterious       Physical       entity,         which
  includes the other two.


            Very often when          we    have    the vision        of       the   Divine
  Form, we remember the Name. Ultimately, Name and                                       Form
  become one-identical. It is very difficult to realise that Name
  itself is Form. The Infinite must be invoked with a devotional
  heart,     But itis very difficult to entertain such devotion-such


                                           259
                                                                Elixir for Life



a passionate      ionging   for    the Lord. It is    only the company of
Saints    that can induce it. ”


                                     (41)
             How to Intensify Concentration ?

         When a    disciple       asked    Sri Gurudeva    as    to how to
make concentration soulful,             he explained :


         5 Patanjali has defined Yoga            as Citta-vrtti-nirodha- or
control of    the mental flow. It is also true that mind becomes
steady    by the control of Praia         through the practice of Pranda-
yama or     breath-control.       But    this   method   does     not      bring
about     a change    in the quality of the mind.         This        is really a
Process    from    the   Bottom.         Trataka etc.    are    all     external
processes.



         But there isa process from the Top which is really
more important. Concentration through devotion is a superior
process. A devotee meditates on Nama with his heart filled
with devotion      and attains the vision of God. In the ‘ Bottom
to Top’ process mentioned above. the physic becomes God.
That process is slightly more practical, no doubt. But it may
not necessarily lead to God. On the other hand, in the ‘ Top
to Bottom’ process, God becomes God. It begins from the
very beginning. For undergoing the process of Hatha-Yoga,
our physic must be strong. But for devotional meditation,
and concentration, ordinary constitution is sufficient.

         Proper time and place are also necessary, for good
concentration.       But growth of            mental ardour is of prime
importance. Tivrasathveganaih 05011140. 11 all depends upon the
fervour. Our earnest passion for spiritual welfare, should
gush up like a fountain towards God. Such a warm zeal can
be developed through (i) Discrimination and (ii) Holy company.

         i) Intelfectual study of the literature of Saints will be
                                        260
Rambhau Maharaj



of some use to facilitate discrimination.            But along withit
meditation on Nama should be necessarily performed. Other-
wise we won’t be able to understand clearly the real signi-
ficance of such literature. The expression of            an experience
can be properly understood only by              those who        have got
such an experience, or enjoyed it. Others won’t. The other
day, Master Krishnarao sung the Abhazga of Juanesvara viz.
6 Krishna hala ka re ° ।10५५ can he understand its real meaning?
This Abhisga of three lines cannot be understood even by
three hundred scholars


       To understand the real secret grandeur of Paramartha-
 Spiritual experience,       the literature of all the Saints of the
 world must be properly studied. And the unity of experience
 presented in    it should    be ascertained.


        ii)    This discrimination should be associated with the
 Company of Saints for         developing    its   efficacy.    These two
  would greatly help to intensify          devotion and zeal of the
  seeker. [t is only when the intensity reaches a stage in which
  the seeker is prepared to sacrifice everything for the Lord, that
  he would have the experience of the Spiritual Energy.


       Spiritual Energy descends through Saints like Jiianesvara
  and others like him. Tney possess a Reservoir of Spiritual
  Energy which oozes down through them.             Spiritual   knowledge
  flows unconsciously        through them. The company of such
  Saints intensifies our fervour.     Even an      exchange of     thought
  with them will be of great help.         Their mere presence also is
   quite enough Even a graceful glance of their Karma- drsti
  would be valuable. But it is not practicable. Things have to be
   realised or achieved by ourselves.


                                    (42)
                     The Triple Confluence


          In    the course     of   conversation     there was     once a


                                     261
                                                                 Elixir for Life


 teference    to   the   Triveni Savigath of Prayag where’there is a
 confluence of        three rivers- Gariga.        Yamuna and Suraswati
 “twa manifest and one hidden. At this Sri Gurudeva remarked :
   There isa       spiritual Triple Confluence.        Do you know ? God,
 Devotee     and    Nama    form       this   Triple Confluence. Of them,
 two   are   visible like Ganga, Yamuna,          and one     is invisible like
 Saraswati. Normally Devotee and Nama are manifest and
 God is unmanifest,-hidden. In the second stage, Devotee
 क्त God ( क - Form) are manifest and Néma is hidden.
 While    in the third stage,      Nama and Riipa (God) are manifest
 and   the   Devotee goes          underground,         Sri   Maharaj once
 remarked : * Though the          Saints      depart   from   the world,   the

 Rtipa experienced by them remains as before.’’ Thus God,
 Devotee and Nima          form   a    Triple Confluence in all the three
senses.    When the      Devotee merges in the Lord, God and Nama
 alone remain. This       is a Confluence of a higher stage. ”




                                      (43)

               Meditation on World as God.


         About the Pantheistic conception of ^“ World is God '"
Sri Gurudeva once observed : ‘‘ [{ is not enough to consider
that God has assumed the beautiful form of the world. It must
be directly experienced. To realise the Power that controls
and guides the Universe, 8 different Sadhana is required. To
observe God in everything and every event in the Universe, is
8 meditation of a higher quality. God is the beginning and end
of the Universe. This fact must be actually experienced.
Before our meditation passes from the mental to the spiritual
realisation, the process in the middle is extremely difficult
“nay, it may even be considered to be practically impossible.
To pass from idea to reality is more an ontological argument
than a spiritual reality. Meditation on Nama alone is an easy
means for its realisation.”



                                      262
Rambhaw Maharai




                               (44)
                  Meditation on Virtues.


      Sri Gurudeya further continued : ‘*Very often meditation
on virtues also is recommended. The Theosophists meditate
on virtues like Abhaya-Fearlessness, Satva-samsudhi- Purity etc.
“ Today | shall be fearless, charitable.            | shall be straight-
forward. ” Such is their repeated auto-suggestion for a number
of days, till they feel that they have assimilated the respective
virtue. Aristotle says : ‘Character is produced or formed by the
repetition of the same act.’ Such meditation           and practice of
virtues becomes a basis for future spiritual achievement. That
is all. 1115 Sadhana has nu more value than that.”


       Really we must perceive God          in all beings,-in every-
thing. We must be able to see and perceive Him both with eyes
shut and open. Spiritual vision is supersensuous. A blind man
sees the vision better as there is nothing to blur it.


       Unless we have a vision of God, we             won’t attain the
 powers and virtues. On the other hand the possession of 11859
 powers and virtues will   facilitate   spiritual    realisation   Thus
 Ethics and Mysticism are inter-dependent. Ethical           and. Spiri-
tual growth meet in God. They meet in Infinity. There ‘is never
4 straight line. So parallel lines meet in Infinity.

directly to mysticism and not to mythology, like other saints.

experienced.”’

                                   (50)
                        Company of Saints


      Referring to his remark regarding the ‘ Service of Saints’
Sri Gurudeva further observed. * A saint himself is God. God
Himself is saint. Hence service of a Saint is service of God. Our
daily meditation should be coupled with the holy company                          of
saints. Then     alone will      it bear proper fruit.           It     is    in the
company of saints that we would realise the real value of
 meditation     If we   try to live in their company for good many
days and observe their behaviour minutely we would under-
stand how they hive realised            thair     identity with         God     and
 possess His Glory.


       Take for intance, my owncase. It               was      the year        1909
 or 1910.     1 wasthen meditating daily for 7 hours: 2 hours in

 and 2 hours at night (from 11P. M.to1A                   M     ). | carried on

 without the aid of an alarm clock. Once sri N.S.                 Lokur        asked

                                                                               I

 awoke exactly at 3-43 and woke him up. Such psychological

  an important occurrence.


        Once during that period,             I! happened        to pay a        visit
  to Incagiri. Sri Bhausaheb Maharaj knew the method of                           my
  meditation.    Still, one day he addressed’me               in this        manner:
  6 What    is the use of mere meditation
                                        ? We                  should seek the
  company of saints. Then we would                realise     its real worth.’

                                                                             Elixziz for Life



Iwas        greatly        rion plussed             and     surprised        to hear    this

         Sri Maharaj   performed his meditation regularly. He

the morning, 1 hour at noon, 3 hours in the evening and
                                                     2 hours
at night.    He       rarely had any sleep. In fact he never needed
it.   During    the       month of Sravana, he used to live on one
dried date per day. At Incagiri, he used to take a few morsels
of food only. Such was tne austere life he led. Still, so
long as his Sadguru -Sri Nimbargi Maharaj was alive, he
never failed to see him at least once a week and have the
pleasure and benefit of his inspiring company. He thus, received
the inspiration and guidance of his Master for well-nigh 25
years, before he could attain the higher reaches of spiritual
experience      ”’

                                 (६4)
Spiritual Experience alone Brings Peace & Joy

        I have always believed that the function of philosophy
is for the consolidation and consummation of spiritual experi-
ence, and it is only the acquisition of this spiritual experience
which makes a man worthy of being the handiwork of God.
The world is torn with dire conflicts today. There is no hope
for humanity except on the basis of spiritual experience whose
power, when writ       large   upon the   world, can     assuage ascer-
bated feelings, reconcile warring         interests, and make huma-
nity a true mirror of the peace, te joy and the glory which is
in God.
                                               (Massage : July 1941 )


                                (55)
     Spiritual Unity through Spiritual Religion


       Sri Swami deserves to be heartily              congratulated   on
 his very happy idea of holding an ‘‘ All Faiths Conference ”
 to bring together men of all kinds of religious belief, ard
 creed, on   the   same   intellectual    platform,    with a view to
 bringing about real      understanding,      harmony      and_    peace,
 between communities in India in           general and     Karnatak in
 particular. For, it    is only’ the spiritual unity of all       commu-
 nities and creeds that is     of an abiding and permanent nature;
 while all groups based on material principles are but superficial
 and short - lived, as they are not sufficiently broad-based and
 selfless in their nature.                           न


       Such latter trends of thought deserve to be corrected
 by abroad and fundamentally unifying             principle. And this
 we cannot find. anywhere else except          in the spiritual nature
 of man. Men are generally misled by false ideologies and
 values in life. These valueshave to be transvalued                10.116
 light of what would be permanently useful                and beneficial

                                   279
                                                         Elixir for bile




to   the    whole humanity      without any     distinction    of   caste,
creed ornationality.      It   is only by     realising the essential
unity of human      nature     and   thereby establishing     the father-
hood   of    God   and   the   brotherhood    of man   that     the   reaj
good of humanity can be achieved. This is the ideal preached
and practised by all saints and sages and prophets of the
world in the past. Spiritual Religion, the creed of all saints
of the world, can alone save us from all separatist, disor-
ganizing and dissipating tendencies and forces.
                                            ( Message : 29-4-1978 ).

                      (7)
   Nature & Spiendour of Spiritual Experience.

    1.    The Spiritual Power is not generated in ourselves by
          ourselves. It must descend. It may be regarded as sclf-
          generated to some extent.

    2.    Every man has to gain the spiritual experience for
          himself. The experience has tocome from within.
          Your experiences are due to internal stimulation.

    3.    In a spiritual seeker, on account of             such   internal
          stimulation the spiritual fluid in         the spinal chord
          rises up-to Brahma randhra in the brain

    4.    This fluid    is the   external   essence of the soul. Ina
          spiritual man the fluid gains spiritual          energy. This
          fluid   is the governing    factor   and    it   is the nearest
           physical material for self-manifestation.

     5.   The spiritual experience is weighed exactly in propor-
          tion to the character. The real nature of oneself is
           known to oneself or to God.

     6.    In spiritual experience there is some            fixed   centre
           around which it grows. The central point is quite
           steady.All further experiences evolve from this central
           nucleus and revolve round it. Nothing can move with-
           Out a nucleus.

     7.    Mystical experience is        continuous and       permanent.
           Perpetuity and continuity are the chief criteria of
           its reality. God does not come on holidays only.
           Mystical  experience flows continuously like the
           stream of ariver. It will inundate or flood on some
           occasions.

     8.    The Spiritual Vastu is capable of infinite number of
           forms and it must subjugate         and give us comfort.


                                   287
                                              Jowels of Thought



      In   the experience of the pearls,   colours develop and
      one colour gives place to another; the brilliant black
      is interpreted   es ‘too much light is darkness’.

10    Because of the spiritual experience,    every nerve-cell
      begins to vibrate with the name of God. You see and
      hear by brain instead of eye and ear.

11.   Peace and     Joy are the natural results of spiritual
      experience. They are not attitudes to be attained by
      practice. Peace, Joy have antithetical equanimity.
      Generally Joy is fundamentallya matter of experi-
      ence. Peace is difficult to be had. Joy requires less of
      self-control, while Peace requires more of it. The
      experience of Joy itself is divine. To control and curb
      it is hypocracy. Peace is one of the aspects against
      Joy.

12.   What is Mukti ? To be a participant in God’s Great-
      ness, Power, Wisdom and Joy is Mukti. We must
      attain it in this life only.

           phico-mystical insight, he sees the unity of the inter-
           nal and external God,       as well as he perceives God in
           all things, and all things in God.


                                  (9)
                         Marathi        Saints


     1.    Tha great mystics of Maharashtra have produced a
           literature which shall continue to be the wonder of all
            humanity, which cares at all for an expression of
            mystical thought in any country without distinction
            of creed, caste or race.                            अ


        2. Jianegwara is the type of intellectual mystic; Nama-

                                  289
                                             Jewels of Thought



     deva heralds the democratic age; Ekanitha synthesises
     the claims of worldly and spiritual life; Tukérama’s
     mysticism is most personal; while Ramadisais the
     type of active saint.

3.   JfAnadevais a Saint           who appears tous from the
     beginning     to the end of his spiritual career, as a
     full-fledged Saint, a Saint not in the making but one
     already made...       Jnanadeva is alight that dazzles
     too much      by its brilliance.

4.   [010206५8 represents the emotional side of spiritual
     life. Ni&imadeva’s insistence upon the significance
     and efficacy of the Name of God is the strongest of
     all the Saints.

5.   Ekanatha was a Saint,while he was yet a house-holder.
     He has brought about a unique reconciliation bet-
     ween worldly and spiritual life unattained either
     before   or   afterwards.

6.   It was principally Ekanitha who made the ideas
     of Vedanta familiar to the men inthe street. With
     Jiianadeva philosophy had reigned in the clouds;
     with Ekanatha it came upon the earth and dwelt
     among    men.


7.   Tukdrdma was the citizen of the world and for that
     matter a citizen of the spiritual world... He not
     merely realised God himself but brought God-reali-
     sation within the easy reach of all.

8.   Ramadasa called people’s minds to the performance
     of duty, while the heart was 10 be always set on
     God. Rimadasa tells us time and again...it is only
     when our efforts are backed by devotion that they
     are   likely to succeed.

9.   While Namadeva and Tukdrama... called back the

                             290
Ramhhan   Maharaj



          attention of men from irreligion                to religion, Raéma-
          dasa raised upon       the foundation of               religious faith
          an edifice of national      greatness.

   10.    Tukdrama devoted his           entire    life     to    the    spiritual
          upliftment of humanity;          Ekanatha gave himself over
          to social reform;      political achievement redounded to
          the credit     of Ramadda@sa; while Ji#aneswara                   spent
          his life in utilising his devotional temperament for
          the mystical upliftment of the world.


                                  (10)
                         Kannada Saints


          Karnatak     Mystics   occupy avery high               place     among
          the great     God-realisers all    over the world              From my
          study of     Marathi and Hindi          Mystics,        |    can assure
          you, that Kannada       Mystics stand ona                   level, which
          is in   no    way inferior to that of the other Mystics.
          In away, we may say,             that     in     many ways they
          stand even on a higher level . They have contributed
          a good deal to the world’s              mystical       thought.

          These great Kannada Mystics evidently divide them-
           selves into two schools, the Saivite and the Vaisnavite
           ... | may point out that the Sesa is welcome both to the
           Saivas and the Vaisnavas;Saivas make Sesa into a neck-
          lace which decorates neck of their God,Siva and Vaisn-
           avas look upon Sesa as the resting couch of Visnu. So,
           it is Sesa who reconciles these two schools of thought.

          * By the expression Haridas, we must understand none
           else but Purandardas.’’? Thus does Vydsriya praise
           his disciple.... He began with Saguna, later equated
           the Saguna with Nirguna and             ultimately he became
           a Yogi and     a Mystic.

          One of the greatest of Karnatak Mystics and                     for that


                                   291
                                            Jewels of Thought



matter   of the whole    world,     Mahipati, is   rarely sur-
passed    in   his   vivid   descripticn   of   the   spiritual
experience.    His heights     of   spiritual   experience, his
profundity of thought, and his powerful style, leave an
everlasting impression on the mind of the reader.

Kanakadéas seems to have had wonderful intellect even
though he belonged to the so-called lower communiy.
He   was undoubtedly a great devotee.

In one of the best songs in Kannada literature, Vijaya-
 das  has beautifully expressed his spiritual expe-
rience.,.This splendid poem gives us, in brief, the
whole history of spiritual life.

Sarpabha#sana was a very humble man. He was a
brilliant, poetical as wellas a mystical writer.
Nijaguna Sivayogi wasa great philosopher as well
as a Mystic.

                          Welcome Address


                        Presented   to Sri Gurudeva
      RAMCHANDRA DATTATRAYA RANADE,                   M, A; D. Litt;
by   the   students     and the   staff of the   Parashuram   Bhau High
Sohool, Jamkhandi,       on 3rd July 1956, the     seves.ieth birth    anni-
versary     of Revared Gurudeva,
                               )


Reyered Gurudeva,

           At    this Amrta   Mahotsava of our Sovereign Saint, we,
the students and the staff of this ancient institution feel
supreme joy in extending  our’ heartiest welcome to you, at
your Alma Mater. We hope and pray for more such happy
returns.


       This blissful day of your seventieth birth anniversary
revives gloriously proud meimcries of old. associated with
your student life in the school. The year 1902 made history,
by giving us, in you, our first Shankar Seth Scholar, ranking
 second         at   the Matriculation       Examination,   in the     whole
 province. Further, your winning at the M.A. Examination in
 1914,     the Chancellors’s      Gold Medal, a most coveted prize,


                                       295
Rambhau Maharaj




in the Bombay University, brought                     greater glories    to your
Alma Mater. Your high erudition and astounding versatility,
peep out in every page of more than half a dozen enduring works,
produced by you. To-day, your word is a gospel and your
mystic touch turns every thing into 91४1 1€ gold. The East
and the West combine              in   admiring and adoring            you.


      Ever Since your studenthood in this institution, you
have been the darling of your Alma Mater, your Great Guru,
 Sri Samartha 81152160                 Maharaj and the Supreme Lord.
The life Divine you have been living, is a perennial source
of inspiration to us and to posterity. Revered Gurudeva, we
 have in you a Master Mystic, having a rare happy, har-
 monious combination of Divine simplicity and serenity.
 Aptly had your learned Principal Bain pronounced words
 about you: “ ४०५ are one of the six greatest men of the
 ४४०10.? We, the young Parashuramians, had prayed for the
 dawn of this blissful day;              and our
                                     beloved Gurudeva,you
 have fulfilled our longing by giving us your Darshana to
 our heart's fill.


        Our heads bow down at Your Venerable Feet, devoutly
 asking for your     benign blessings to enkindle in us the Divine
 Spark; for, we      feel sure,         then,    of    ushering in a still more
 glorious future     for    our    institution,        turning   it   into a   big
  Spiritual Centre tov.


        Our Most      Venerable Gurudeya,

                                          We ever remain,
                     Yours        in   ardent    admiration,     deep devotion

                            The        Students and the Staff of the
                           Parashuram Bhau High School, Jamkhandi.

                                 (2)
           Attainment of the Vision Divine


                  ( By: Dr 5. Radhakrishnan ).
                            ( His Message

                       On the occasion of

THE THIRD PUNYATITHI OF GURUDEVA RANADE)

                      ( 5th of June, 1360)

        | am honour2d by the invitation to say 8 few words on
the   release of the late    Professor R. D. Ranade’s last work on
‘© Pathway to God     in Kannada       literature ’’ on the 511 June,
which   happens to be the      anniversary of his passing away. |
enjoyed his friendship and affection from the time | met         him
in 1925 at the first Indian Philosophical Congress in Calcutta.
His simplicity. his integrity, his sweet and affectionate nature
impressed all who came into contact with him.


        For many years he taught philosophy           at Poona,    at
Amainer and at Allahabad. Philosophy for him, was not
                                                    a
Profession buta consuming. passion.
                                 He thought,             not merely
with his intellect but with his whole life.



                                 297
Rambhsau Moaheray



        He had remarkable linguistic equipment. Apart from his
mastery of English, he knew           Greek and            German and had 8.
command of Hindi, Marathi and Kannada. He made                      very valu- .
able contributions to our knowledge of mysticism in                    Marathi,
Hinai   and    Kannada      literatures.       He
                                        expressed his deepest
convictions in words and ways intelligible to the ordinary man.


        Professor Ranade tells us on the very first page of this
book that ५ mysticism is a way of spiritual life; which binds
all humanity together. ” Religion, at its highest, is a matter of
direct experience of ultimate reality, an experience which is
intuitive, super-sensuous and different from normal modes of:
thought. On the strength of that experience we cannot make
ontological affirmations. The intellectual apprehension and
formulation of-transcendent truth belong toa different order
than the experience which they attempt to explain. The imme-
diacy is not there,       the   conviction     of finality is     no   present.
The need for uttering the unutterable leads to                    ambiguity of
, 11612066. - Professor    Ranade tells us          that   ‘‘no    real mystic
usually gives expression to his own experience. ’? An American
Poet, Emily Dickinson says ; ** Tell the truth but tell it slant”.

        The way to attain the experience is by meditation                   ard
prayer. All the religious thinkers ask us to know tne deepest in
us.




             Ninna nijava ni nodo (know thyself )


        Know the truth of your Self. God dwells in the silence,
 the cave,  the guha of the heart. He is Guhesvara. Without a
 retreat into the self, true human life  is not 00531 213. The
 Buddha withdraws into the forest. Jesus goes apart into the
 desert for forty days. Muhammad               gets   into his tent.


        Professor   Ranade- gives          a    detailed     account of     the


                                    298
                                                        Vision Divine



di'ferent   modes of approach       adopted by the saint-singers
of   Karnataka.    There are a few references to his own experi-
ences.

         The God-realised souls form a blessed community-Anu-
bhavamantapa working with love for afflicted mankind. History
is the progressive embodiment of the vision of human brother
                                                           -
hood     culminating   ina   society of   free spirits, a body of men
dedicated     toseeking truth.      Ranade spent his life in     the
pursuit of this ideal.       He reminds us of the verse in Sanka-
racarya’s Mohamudgara :



                  guru-caranambujua-nirbhara-bhaktah
                    samsarad ucirad bhava muktan
                  sendriya-manasa-niyamdad eva
                    draksyasi nijahrdayastham devam


Cultivate a strong devotion to-the lotus-feet of your preceptor,
thereby get freed soon from 58713218. Only by a control of
the senses andthe mind does one attain a vision of              the
Divine seated     in one’s heart.
                           (3)
             Harbinger of Renaissance.


                  ( by : Dr. V. K. Gokak )

      Dr R 0. Ranade was one of the gifted sons of India
who achieved great distinction in several departments of
life - educational, intellectual, constructive and spiritual.
Karnatak was the home of his physical and spiritual birth and
evolution. Maharastra and Utter Pradesh provided the setting
for his career as a professor and educationist. The world came
to know him through his ‘ Constructive Survey of Upanisadic
Philosophy.’’ Numerous pupils and devout disciples grew in the
intellectual and spiritual sunshine that he scattered so prodi-
gally around. He had his own share of the cross and the crown,
the fortunes and misfortunes of life. He bore the cross cheer-
fully and wore the crown with a great and deep sense of
humility. Dr Ranade was as great as a philosopher as he was
a mystic. His influence in the circles of the elite in India
is due to the remarkable combination of two distinctive gifts—
philosophic discrimination and vision.

                             300
                                                    Harbingers,
                                                             of Renaissance



       Dr. Ranade was an illustration of the Indian Rena-
issance and he dida great deal constructively, intellectually and
spiritually, to promote it further       towards its
                                              own fulfilment.
He founded spiritual centres in Nimbal, Sangli and Allahabad.
He made contributions of enduring significance to Indian phi-
losophic literature. And he left behind him a large and cultured
fraternity of disciples practising       a    living spiritual        discipline
which had been handed down from master                 to disciple           in    the
Past and which found in him its most illustrious exponent and

representative.    `


       Nothing else brings better the rich. authenticity and
Pervasiveness of       the Renaissance       than    the emergence of               a
  hole tribe of saints and pioneers          simultaneously          and     conti-
nuously in all parts of India.    The richness and         variety         of this
emergence strikes a student of the Renaissance                 not    less    pro-

foundly than the advent of Shakespeare and               his tribe which
mada   Elizabethan      England   a   nest      of    singing    birds.           The
humanist and the sceptic will continue to               turn    his back on
this splendour. urging that what is hailed as light is really                      a
relapse into the ‘‘primeval darkness” of the Vedic times. But
the student of the Ranaissance who has responded 10 the
fusion of reason-and imagination, of intellect and intuition,
of work and worship, is sure to be fascinated by the. infinite
wealth that it has brought to India.            ४

  , ` ' The self-discovery of the East, the meeting of East and
 West in a grand moment of synthesis, tha presentation of
_this synthetic vision in English which is a world language, the
 coming together of the occidentals and orientals who have
 consanguinous spirituality,the reinterpretation of a living 90111
 tual tradition so as 10 bring -it -in line with the modern
 world ~ these are some of.the features that characterise ‘the
 Indian Renaissance.       This is amply illustrated in the life of
 Dr. Ranade.                                                                             :




                                  301
Rambhau Maharaj


      A    te-interpretation of    ancient and             mdieval     Indien
poetry is also a feature of the New Age. If Dr. Ranade gave
us a classical and scholarly account of ancient Indian thought
10 his Constructive Survey of Upanisadic Philosophy, his
volumes on the “Pathway10  s God’? may be described as
romantic in their approach to medieval Indian poetry. It is 8.
fascinating experience to read the interpretations of the
poetry of the mystics of North India. Maharastra and Karna-
“vak. He shows there how the experience embodied in this
 poetry is the same as that of mystics all over the world. Many
 obscure songs suddenly spring 10 life in the revalatory light
 that he sheds on them by referring frequently to his own
 experience. This is specially true of the account he gives of
 the mystic poets of Karnatak. He penetrates through various
 philosophic terminologies, and diverse credal formulations to
 the core of experience that lies enshrined within them and
 brings out the universal significance that underlies various
 forms and beliefs. Tnis serves to underline the unity of Indian
 thought that persists through a bewildering variety of forms.


       The frail body of Dr. Ranade houses a great soul                He was
 8 great builder. teacher and scholar and 8              serene philosopher
 and mystic. For several ४९315 he       hardly   lived       on    any other
 nourishment but tea    But he needed no other food :


                  For he on honeydew hath fed

                  And drunk the milk of paradise.



          | was privileged to come into contact           with    Dr. Ranade
  on a few occasions. As an undergraduate            in    Dharwar      as far
  back as 1928, | thrilled to his eloquence when he               lectured on
  the Upanisads. Through his      close   disciples        who       were   my
  friends, and through Prof. (४. ©, Damle,           ।    could      get vivid
  glimpses of the manner in which he was evolving into.a great
 Seer. He presided over a lecture that           |       delivered     on   Sri


                                  302
                                         Harhinger of Renaissance



Aurobindo at the residence of Srimant     Rajasaheb   of Sangli.
As the then Dean of the Arts Faculty of the Karnatak Univer-
sity, | arranged for one of his extension lectures. | had the
honour of receiving him at my residence at Oharwar.And when
he passed eway, 1 had a strange intimation of it in a dream,
a few hours before | read about it in my morning newspaper. 1
treasure these memories of the great man and [ am sure that
thousands of individuals all over the country do so in their own
way.



       The dawn of the Renaissance is slowly but      inevitably
breaking into day. 1 salute Dr. Ranade as one of the harbingers
of tuis Polar Dawn.

                       A Loving Personality

                     ( By Professor George           B.   Burch
                                                              )

      ( Professor George 8.. Burch teaches philosophy at
Tufts College. Metford, Massachusetts. In 1953-54 he and
his family were in India,           to which         Professor      Burch      came to
discuss     philosophy       with     Indian         philosophers.        prominent
among whom was the late                   R.    D. Ranade.         In   sending       this
article    Professor     Burch writes :-


          “It   is    customary,     when
                                       8 0168६             man dies, to publish
eulogies of him which,             written      under      the      stress      of     the
occasion,       are often uncritical           and   exiggerated          It    may be
better to wait a year or two. If                     he still seems great in
retrospect,      his life can be          appraised       in   a   more        objective
spirit. 8. 0. Ranade is a man whose stature, in my estimate,
has only grown          10 restrospéct. ”


          We are glad indeed to publish                   this vivid      and_       inter-
esting     account based on         the    author’s own recollections                as   8


                                          304
                                                          Loving Personality


tribute    to the   late R. 0. Ranade        Ed.) १४

          Ramchandra      Dattatraya Ranade was born               in   1886 at
Jamkhandi,      given     a   mantra   by a guru named           Bhausahib at

the age of      fourteen and          educated at Deccan College. He
acquired only a distaste for Philosophy                  here,    where. the
Professor     of    Philosophy        assigned    0       reading        except
Aristotle’s Ethics, Wallace’s Kant, Mill’s Logic and Martineau’s
Ethical     Theory,      and    16610160      from the       same _      notes
for   twenty years.      But in other fields he got a fine education.
He specialized      in   mathematics, studied          English    with    Clark
and   learned Sanskrit from Pathak. He learned the techniques
of scholarly research from Rawlinson, to whom he taught
Sanskrit in exchange for tutoring in Greek. His most influ-
ential teacher was F.W. Bain, later Professor of Economics
at All Souls’ College,          an Englishman with a deep appre-
Ciation of Hinduism, whose beautiful stories of tha Rajput
era, written in the form of pretended translations trom Indian
originals, evoke visions of India even by their titles ( ^ Digit
of {16 Moon. A Heifer of the Dawn, In the Great God’s Hair,
Tne Ashesof a God). When Bain left Deccan Collegea,
spokesman for the students said, in a public eulogy, that
they had learned more philosophy from him than from the
Professor of Philosopiay and more literature than from the
Professor of Literature. [६ was from Bain that Ranade
received avision of eternal beauty and truth.

       While in college he began his life-long habit of devoting
 three hours a day to meditation (even during examination
periods, as one awed disciple told me without really expecting
me to believe it ). 10 1903 the year he received his B. A. from
 the University of Bombay, he began having the mystical
experiences which cor:tinued throughout his life. At first he
found these experiences confusing. Ye went to Banaras to

          ‡ॐ 1015 article was first published in the August
 1959 Number of Aryan Path. This introductory note is by
 the Editor of      Aryan     Path.


                                       305
Rambhau Maharaj

discuss them with            the   well-known         Annie    Besant of the.
Theosophical Society and                she assured      him   that they were
real.


          He became a fellow of Deccan College after graduating,
was appointed curator of            manuscripts         in 1912, and    received
 the M. A. in 1914          During this period he became interested in
 philosophy, first of all          in   Aristotle’s     philosophy.    With   his
 command of         Greek,    he   undertook      the    ambitious     project of
 making an exhaustive commentary on Aristotle’s Metaphysics.
 This project did not get very far, but it made a good start. The
 Metaphysics begins with a critique of the pre-Socratics, and
 the beginning of the proposed commentary                   produced a     series
 of     articles,   eventually published        separately on      various pre-
 Socratic philosophers. These studies had a considerable                   influ-
 ence on his later thought.


            In 1914 he was appointed Professor of Philosophy at the
 quasi-monastic Fergusson College in Poona. 11                  1916, when his
 friend the philanthropist Pratap Seth founded the Indian                   Insti-
 tute of Philosophy at ⁄47 21067, Ranad2                gave   technical   advic®
  and selected the books for            thelibrary. Academically this was
 the happiest period of his life.He later recalled with pleasure his
 intimate association with the excellent students                 at   Fergusson
 College Personally it was a tragic period. The great influenza
  epidemic of 1218 took his mother and his wife, and left him ina
 state of poor health from which he never completely                   recovered,
  and     which compe'led his retirement six years later.


            Bhausahib died in 1914, and was succeeded as guru
                                                            by
  Ranade’s fellow disciple Amburao. In 1921 Ranade established
  an     ashrama     inthe outskirts of         the small village of Nimbal.
  ( This is some thirty miles north               of Bijapur, acity which
  Ranade urged         me    to visit, not only to accept         an   invitation
  from one of his disciples but             also to see the Gol Gumbuz, a
  building he considered “ Sublime, ” whereas                  the Taj     Mahal


                                          306
                                                            Loving Personality


was merely ^^ beautiful.’?        )    When Amburao died,       Ranade       was
persuaded, although reluctantly, to undertake the                  responsibi-
lities of    the guruship.    He        moved     to the ashrama         in 1924,
 assured the spiritual guidance of his former fellow                 disciples,
 and also began initiating disciples himself. | was told in                 1954
 that he then had about 2,000 disciples, living in various parts
of India    For them he was their gurudeva. their teacher, to                  be
reverenced like a god      His three years at Nimbal            were      fruitful

not only spiritually but also scholastically.              Besides the works
On the   pre-Socratics,      he       published   a   comparative    study of
Greek and Sanskrit, an edition of Carlyle’s essay, two books
On Indian philosophy, a four-volume Source                  Book    of    Maha-
rashtra Saints in Marathi,a monumental Constructive Survey of
Upanishadic Philosophy and a volume on The Creative                       Period
for a proposed eight-volume history of Indian philosophy


           His health     somewhat            improvad;    he   accepted      an
appointment as       Professor of           Philosophy in the University of
Allahabad     in   1927   WHestayed          there, as professor and some-
times dean, for nineteen years. but he never enjoyed teaching
there as well as he had enjoyed teaching at Poona. He lived in
abig rambling        bungalow          in   the suburbs.    When । went to
Allahabad for the Kumbha Mela in 1954, although Ranade was
not there,    | stayed    in this house as Pratap Seth’s guest,
browsed in his fine philosophical library ( with its                complete
set of Mind), and met some philosophy students living there.
Ranade’s book on Mysticism in Maharashtra, basedon the
earlier source Book, was published in 1933, and he continued
his research inthe        field of       popular mysticism by extending
 it to the oral tradition in Hindi. Wnenever he met anyone,
‘in any walk of life, he would ask him if he knew any songs,
‘and if he got in reply a song with any spiritual significance,
he would write it down. {0 this way                   he gathered material
for his book on Hindi mysticism, published in 1954 under
the title Pathway to Godin Hindi Literature. Eventually he
added a volume on    Kannada mystics, thus completing a


                                        307
Rambhau        Maharaj



trilogy on      the mystical traditions in three                 vernaculars with
which     he    was acquainted.


         He retired from          teaching      at sixty,          but        stayed at
Allahabad       another     year as Vice-Chancellor of             the University.
After 1947        he    resided   at the     Nimbal     Ashrama, but usually
returned to his Allahabad home for the cold seas
                                                                  on. His personal
life   became     extremely ascetic.          | was   told that          he    gave    up
eating entirely, except           for drinking tea with milk and sugar.
He devoted his time to             meditation,        scholarly       research        and
writing    and     the spiritual    direction     of his        disciples.      It    was
at     Nimbal    that    I met him in 1954.


  +   When | went to India to study Vedanta, seve
                                                  ral persons
spoke to me of Ranade as the best teacher of mys
                                                 tical philo-
sophy. This was not            my chief interest, ०५६ |           became        curious
about the man personally. A physics professor described
                                                         him
as the most advanced person he knew. and
                                           refused to express
an opinion as to whether he was a jiva
                                       n-mukta. | was warned
Not to try to visit him at the ashrama, where the
                                                  life                         was    too
 austere fora      Westerner. | did          have doubts about               wanting to
 visit him, but on very different grounds. Hindu gurus
                                                                              as aclass
have 8 mixed           reputation, some       times   seeming ( at least to a
Westerner ) to be arrogant, pompous or conceited.                        |    had heard
 of gurus, including quite famous Ones, who kept                    themselves in
 seclusion, refusing to see         their own disciples,           let       alone    visi-
 tors. But | taok a chance, wrote Ranade  a letter                       asking       per-

         The man | met was the opposite of what | had                          expected
“Small, slight and frail, a mere wisp of               aman whom you would

                                                     Loving Parsonality



 impossible in this humble man, who kept his perspective and

whom he was divine. He was frank and friendly. eager to talk
with me, to learn as well as    to    teach,    to   discuss       both   his
intellectual interests and   mine.    After    telling    me   about      his
education, he asked me to tell him about         mine. Rapport            was
established when we discovered        a   common         interest    in the
Pre-Socratics, and we exchanged offprints in             this field.      We
became close friends immediately. 1 did not get the impressions
however, that this was anything special about me.              I    believe
that he was that way with everybody. But, for all his humili-
ty, a visitor at Nimbal could never be mistaken            as to which
man was the guru. Ranade’s spirituality shone clearly through
every look, word and act. He did not have to pretent to be a
saint, because he obviously was one.


      The ashrama was a group of five small stone buildings,
The only neighbours were a ^“ criminal-caste ”’ group living in
eight mud huts - fine, dignified people who, as | found, would
do favours four me but would not take baksheesh. Nearby
were a miraculous never - failing well which Ranade had dug
on aspot revealed ina vision after the old well did fail,
and aten-foot pit into which Ranade used to go for his
meditation on days when the ashrama was crowded. Living in
the ashrama were Ranade, his second wife, his daughter, 115 1४४0
small grandchildren and aboui fifteen disciples. They came from
different social backgrounds: 2 young raja, a retired Postmaster
General, college professors, doctors ( one of whom Ranade’s
physician, was trying to get him to supplement his tea with
orange juice ), lawyers, business m2n. clerks, the local station-
master, a Harijan ( ५५10, - coming to Ranade in distress when
his children were starving on his forty rupee school-teacher’s
 Salary, was assisted by him to get a hundred -rupee social
 worker’s position ): Tney had been            drawn to religion by
‘various influences-one, a Madras doctor, through the frus-
 trations of bureaucratic regulations; another, a lawyer with

                                309
Rambhau Maharaj



an international practice, through the company of saintly men
he met during three years in jail. This lawyer said Ranade had

thought| would      prefer to their usual fare            and    other conve-
niences for my comfort. While|            neither       requested      nor espe-
cially wanted      this special attention,| was touched by and
appreciative of this hospitality       toward a self-invited guest.


        The day began at six, when the disciples assembled for
 devotions, chanting a hymu to the guru. We were expected to
 imitate the guru’s practice by meditating               together          for    three
 hours, but actually began leaving          after       about     an       hour. In
 mid-afternoon a bell, indicating          that     Ranade        had       finished
 his own spiritual exercises, summoned us to his                    presence        for
 readings and discussion, followed by the               ceremonial burning
 of camphor, inhaling the         smoke    and     distribution            of prasad.
 Each evening someone gave a talk, and there was a final chant
 before retiring. The hymn to the guru             ( --48}      guru       Jai    Guru
 Jai Guru Jav’’), acconpanied by cymbals, was chanted before
 photographs of Amburao,          Bhausahib       and    the    latter’s guru’s
  tomb (no photograph           of him being available). In their                  own

  when singing “ Jai Guru’, but there was no picture of                            him,
  nor was he himself present at these devotions. It                 any one ever
  made any ggsture of veneration           in his presence,            |     did    not
  observe it.


          Interesting    and edifying      as     these spiritual exercises
  were,    my philosophical        conversations         with     Ranade           were
  more so. His philosoahy, which he called Beatificism, meaning
  the     search   for    Beatitude   as     Self -      realisation,            was      8
   mystical philosophy in the        tradition of        Vishishtadvaita            and
   Bnakti
     ~ marga.            He.   rejected Advaita       and      Jnana-marga             4s
   dangerous teachings opposed to mysticism. One day 8 discipl®


                                      310
                                                      Loving Personality


recited    a   humorous       poem on“ Ten Great Saints,” in which
the    eulogy    of    each    Saintwas qualified     bya statementof
the    defect    in his   sanctity.    The ten   saints   were   Prahlada,
Dhruva,        Narada, Vyasa,        Shuka,   Bhishma, Arjuna, Valmiki.
Hanuman and           Uddhava;    in the case of Shuka the defect was
that   he was an Advaitin. All speculative philosophy, according
to Ranade, is uncertain; all we can know of metaphysics is
that all things come from God               and tend to return    to God.
What      we can know is the Self.


        The means of Self-realization are fourfold. First, moral
behaviour both the prerequisite for, and the evidence of,             true
mysticism. Second, the company of good people - hence the
importance of life in the ashrama, Third,                 a guru. Ranade
rejected the theory, often advanced, that the guru chooses
the disciple, and maintained that the disciple must seek and
choose his guru. (When he told me this, a sudden emotion
swept over me. Had not providence, or Karma, brought me to
                          the most spiritually advanced
this venerable man, probably
person | shall ever know, to whom J was already bound by
ties of mutual affection, in order that               he should be my
spiritual preceptor ? Should I not ask him then and there to
give    me      initiation     ? 1    rejected this   impulse, however,
and in retrospect am sure that [ was right. He could only
have been embarrassed by so intemperate a suggestion,
since initiation doubtless requiresa preliminary discipline,
while from my point of view 1, asa Christian, already have
my satguru in Christ. ) Fourth, meditation-intellectual, moral
and mystical. The all-important thing is love of God, which is
aresponse to his love for us, and this is attracted by the
moral goodness resulting from our own efforts. This, | take it,.
is the “° monkey theory ” of salvation : to be saved we at least
have to hang on. It is by devotion, not deeds or knowledge,
that we are united with God. When, after returning to America,
॥ was asked to give a lecture on contemporary Indian teachers,
I spoke of Vinoba as teaching the way of action, Malkani as

                                      311
Rambhau Maharaj



teaching the way of knowledge              and Ranade as           teaching       the
Way of love.


       To love your family and your friends and, above
                                                           all,
God was Ranade’s doctrine and Ranade’s life.
                                              Spiritual medi-
tation and mystical contemplation were the
                                           central activity of
his daily life He was 8 mystic in the perennia
                                               l tradition of
the mystic saints. Did he          then attain their final             goal of mys-

after! knew him. He told me that he had neve

                                         men.

         Ranade saw       meoff     at    the       Station    with     expressions
of     friendship   and   devotion       and        80   invitation      to    return,

                                              soph                      er- mystic.”

institutions and individuals in India and abroad.

          Much as | appreciate Ranade's                  Spirituand

forgotten. For his ५1501 2165 he was much                     more. For
                                                        Indiahe
 was one of her great men. In India, as also in other
                                                      countries,
 there are many great scholars engaged in various researches,
 many great philosophers with deep insights into
                                                      reality,


                                      312
                                             Loving Personality



many great mystics with ineffable visions, many great teachers
who inspire their pupils, many great souls whose integrity and
personality are radiant But we seldom see one person who is
allof these at once. Such a one was Shri Ranad2, one of
those rare spirits who show us how human nature can be.

        Sri Gurudeva’s Guidance and                             Glory

            ( By : Padmasri Kakasaheb Karkhanis )

                                          (i)
                      My Double Conversion


      During 1910 Sri Gurudev had come to stay in his                      house
at Jamakhandi        for    a   few       days.   His   usual study went       on
there as well   Generally he got his books read by some reader.
His reader at that time, was my friend Sri Nath Mhaskar. He
was then reading           the works of Swami             Vivekanand for him.
Along with him | also used to go to the house of                  Sri    Gurudev
and listen to the talks about spiritual life as well as                 about the
inspiring incidents in the life of Sri Bhausaheb Maharaj. grad-
ually developed 8 liking for them. Tne maxim that company
influences the attitude of man,               proved to be true in      my case
as well. Sri Gurudeva’s (then called Ramabhau) close associa-
tion began      to    produce         a    salutary     transformation    in   my
attitude.


       Sri Ramabhau was then regarded as a brilliant scholar


                                          : 314
                                                   Guidance and Glory



by one and all at Jamakhandi. He had been 8150 3           subject of
loose talk as disciple of Sri Maharaj. | cared very little about
these opinions of the public, either for or against Ramabhau.
As | was daily observing him, | was very well impressed by
his   personality.   During    this   period   |   once   asked   him:
‘““Ramabhau ! Have you seen any Divine Visions?” My concep-
tion of ‘visions’ at that time, was influenced by the descrip-
tions of visions in the Gurucaritra. Sri Gurudev replied to my
question in the affirmative. 1 then requested him to let me
know the nature of one such vision. Thereupon he asked me:
^° Have you read Gita?’ Yes, | replied. ^“ Then you must be
remembering the      verse   ‘Divi siiray sahasrasya’ and others ?
] have got the constant vision of such an effulgent Light
described in it.’’ This reply brought about an entire change
in my traditional conception of a vision. A totally fresh
conception about the same dawned upon me. My notion
about spiritual life underwent a drastic change. | felt an urge
to know the means of getting such visions. With the guidance
of Sri Ramabhau | soon approached Sri Bhausaheb Maharaj and
got myself initiated by him and entered into the blessed fold
of his disciples. This took place a littly later.

       During his stay here, Sri Ramabhau once came to my
house all of a sudden. After some formal talk he asked:
“What is your future programme?” At once | replied: “1 want
to become a Vivekanand. ” Thereupon he quietly said : “ Very
good ! But if you really want to become a Vivekanand, is it
not necessary for you to make the requisite preparation? ” To
this | asked : “What sort of preparation is necessary?” Sri
Ramabhau said: ‘ You will have to receive higher education
in the College. Don’t you think so? Please consider this matter
seriously”. | then said : ‘“Ramabhau [| don’t speak in this in-
direct way. Just tell me frankly whether | should join the
College.’ He replied : ^“ | can only sav that it would be
helpful to you in the pursuit of your ideal. । only wish that
you should think properly about it. ”’ When 1 heard these words
 | immediately told him : ^^ There is no question of thinking

                                315
~Rambhau Maharaj


 now.   I have just decided to join the College.            Only ask     dear
 Anna that
        I wish to join        the    Deccan       College    and   not    the
 Fergusson College    as    the     authorities    there    are hostile    to
 Lokamanya Tilak. ” Sri Ramabhau agreed             to do so and | there-
 after joined the Deccan College.


        One factor in    the incident       still continues to     pain me.
‘1 feel constant repentance for it. Though          Sri    Gurudev was a
 “simple Ramabhau then, | had entertained a very high regard
 for him. But | had not the capacity to know his real greatness.
  Neither did |   know the high stature of Swami               Vivekanand.
  What a fool was!      10 speak like that before such a           towering
  person? This dart still pierces my soul.



                                     (ii)
                     His Spiritual Greatness


         In tha year 1920, I had the good fortune of staying
  with Sri Gurudev at Incagiri. Sri     Gurudev was residing
  then near the Samadhi of 51 Maharaj for the recovery of
  health, for nearly one year. From the spiritual point of view
  that happened to be a blessed year for me. 8838058 I could
   then observe the day to day life of Sri Baba and Sri Gurudev.
   Every minute | could actualiy visualise what penance is like.
   ॥ could also observe there the embodiments of                spirituality.
   1 had the pleasure of hearing from Sri          Gurudev several of his
   brilliant spiritual experiences. | have tried to publish them in
   my recent Marathi book about Sri Gurudeva’s Reminiscences.
   11016 [ propose to shara a couple of them with the readers.


          Once Sri Gurudev told me at Incagiri ~ ‘* So far as my
   personal elevation      is concerned, । have attained the supreme
   spiritual goal. Hereafter, things may take their course according
   to the will of Sadguru.”’ ‘‘ My personal spiritual goal has
   been attained ” means, in the words of Jnanesvar, “ Taralo,
   aralo, 212 uddharalo gurukripe” - “ [ am saved | | am saved !
                                       316
                                                            Guidance and Glory


 1    am liberated through         the grace of Sadguru.           Now it rests
with the       grace of     the Master, to grant me power               to   liberate
 the    world.    ?   Such    is   the significance        of   these    words of
Gurudev.       They show what             a    great spiritual      height      had
been     reached      by him even as far back         as 1920.


      Sri Gurudev generally described his own experiences
through those of other Saints. About his two great works-
“The      Constructive Survey of          Upanisadic        Philosophy ” and
** Mysticism in Maharastra,” he once informed ˆ“ In these two
works.    [ have      not described    a single experience        which       | had
Not enjoyed        already    Ihave    described my own         experience       in

the    words of 1२575     and Saints.’ These very remarks were later
On made by him, about his other two works- “Pathway to God
in    Hindi    Literature ”    and    ^“ Pathway      to    Godin       Kannada
Literature. ? This is aclear          Indication of    the rich variety        and
sublime grandeur of Sri             Gurudeva's spiritual greatness and
glory.

                                           - 1 said, “ What
can J tell you ? Maharaj ( Shri Bhatisanebd                Maharaj ) may tell

                              (iv)
                     “Aversion For Siddhis”

        Shri Gurudeva once told me his experience as follows-
 “‘When | was progressing in my Sadhana, a stage arrived
 when | was able to see the past and future of the person sit-
 ting in front of me.! grew restless thereby and requested the
 Maharaj that | did not want any of such rddhi and siddhi. |
 told him that [ wanted nothing but Bhakti and prayed to him
  to stop all that. After this prayer of me those visions came to
  an end.” All such events happened in the life of Shri Guru-
 deva prior to 1915. He lived thereafter for about 42 years. He
 did not waste even a single breath as he always engaged it in
 N&ama-smarana. So one can easily imagine how much spiritual
 power he must have attained during that long period.

         J participated in the national independence movement
 in November-December 1922 when ! was the chief of the

                                               Guidance and Glory



Svavalambana Rashtriya Pathashala at Chinchawad ( Poona )
| was   sentenced   to   rigorous   imprisonment for four months.
Before | went to the jail, | wrote a few letters, one of which
was for Gurudeva. He used to stay then in the house of Shri
Bhaurao Nad agouda at the village Nimbal. After my sentence
was over, I went to Alandi, had the 44144710 of the samadhi of
Shri Jiidnesgvara and proceeded to Bijapur.On my way! got
१०५८ at Nimbal and went to see Shri Gurudeva Ranade. He
‘old me that even before he received my letter he knew that I
Nas in trouble, and that he had informed Prof. Krishnarao
3ajendragadkar and Shri Jagannatha Lele accordingly. | asked
iim, ^ How did you know that ? ”. He replied, “४९ When | was

                            (6)
                Heart Speaks to Heart
             ( by Sri Gangadharrao Deshpande )


                   Prayer for Peace


      When Guruvarya Rambhau Ranade asked me last night,
to give at least a brief talk this morning,| was greatly puzzled.
] could not decide what I should talk about. During the last
55 years of iny public life. । delivered good many lectures. ॥
have addressed huge gatherings of thousands of persons, even
for two hours at a stretch. But today, | don’t wish to give
such a lecture. | wish to lay bare my heart, to unburden my-
self this morning. It is a sin, no doubt, to talk without inspira-
tion or authority. But it is a greater sin to disobey one’s
Master. Hence | decided to prefer the lesser sin and speak out
my mind as desired by Guruvarya.

       1 have spent the last 55 yearsin national work, in public
service. At first, | worked as a follower of Lokamdanya Tilak,
 during his life-time. After his demise,   | began to work as a

   Note: A tree English rendering of talks during a sittng of
          Sri Gurudev in Mal- Bunglo of H.H. Rajasaheb      Sangli
          on 18-12-1951.


                               320.
                                                       Guidance and Glory


follower of Mahdtmaji. After the departure of Lokamdnya,
there was a keen controversy regarding the correctness and
Propriety of the opinions of both these leaders.               My friends
and fellow workers also differed a good deal about them.               But
I did not bother myself about this controversy. | thought that
Mahétmaji was simply bearing the banner of Lokamanya                  8.0
decided to follow him.


       During the last 55 years, | have worked quite honestly
and sincerely. | have done many good things and at times,
might have done some bad things as well           | possess both merits
and   demerits,   generally   to   be    found   in   ordinary   persons-

possibly in a somewhat intense form. Without being vain, but
with due deference     to my self-respect,            | can claim a lot of
good things to my credit. But,with all that, for the last 4 or 5
years, | have been keenly feeling a need of mental peace, of
inner satisfaction. Really peace is the fulfilment of life. But
in the evening of my life, 1 have been pining for peace. This
mental unrest of mine has greatly upset me. | don’t get sound
sleep at night. So the problem that confronts me is this. While
engaged   in   national work, Lokaménya could               enjoy peace,
Muhatmaji could experience peace. They were not mentally
disturbed like me. Why, then, should | be disturbed like this ?
When |! began to ponder over this problem, | found that the
peace, enjoyed by Lokamanya, was the result of his faith in
God. He had implicit faith in God. Very often [heard him
utter the following words, during his lectures : ‘* If God wills-
1 God blesses.’ At times, he used to conclude his lectures
with the following remark : “ May’ God grant you the will to
act up to instructions given so far. ” In the beginning, | consi-
dered this to be, merely a mode of speech with the elderly
Persons. But later on, | actually asked Lokamanya as to why he
talked about God, in tnis maaner. Lokaminya replied: *‘ Look
here, God is the real do2r: notning can take place, but by His
will. In spiteof our utmost efforts, no work would succeed
®xcept through His Grace.’   | was not very well impressed


                                   321
Rampbhau Maharaj



with this answer then.    Mahatmaji also had a similar faith in
God-nay-it was more Intense than        this. Mahatmuji.   used to
describe God as Truth and   Non-vio'ence, no doubt.      However,
like Lokamanya he also had an implicit faith, in a Mysterious
Power, that transcended everything       and   ruled everything. 1
may say. by the by, this was the main reason that goaded me
10   follow Mahitmaji. Whenever | would launch upon a        fresh
venture, | used to ask myself : ** What would Lokamanya have
done under these circumstances? ? And when | satisfied my-
se!f that he would have done the same thing that had suggested
itself to me, then | used to bagin the work. | never felt any
difference between Lokamanya and Mahitmaji.



        I tell you once again,    that Lokamanya had       an un-
shakable faith in God. | once asked him: * Sir, what will
you do after we get       Swardjya”’? He       replied: If we get
 Swarajya during my life-time,    | shall repair to the banks of
the holy Ganges. take Sanydsa      in the place. where my grand-
father had done so, and spend the remainder of my life, in
meditation on God and contemplation on the Ultimate Reality”’.
But he departed before the advent of Swardajya. Several of my
colleagues also were danied the privilege of having a glimpse
of Swardjya, But fortunately, | could have that privilege. My
 ideal of freeing my country from      the foreign yoke, has been
fulfilled, and now | am breathing the free         atmosphere of
 Swarajya ..... My financial condition also is not 980 . ... |
have earned sufficient fame by now and have a good position
 in society. And after Swardjya, 1 could easily have shone in
 newspaper columns by engaging my-self in similar public
 activities.: However, [am sorry to say that | don‘t have any
 peace of mind.[ don’t quite understand why। should not
 get peace, even though | have been successful in myfamily
 as wellas my public life, and even when! amnot without
 faith in God. | am therefore. anxiously in search of peace
 and tranquility.   | have done good deeds so far, but | must
 confess that I could not rid myself of my defects.        When|

                      t
                                 322
                                                         Heart Sneaks to Heart



 begin to compare my merits’ and defects, | find                            that the
 latter      out-number      the    former. | am stating this, not through
 a   false     sense    of modes'y. | am sincerely unburdening myself

 today, setting aside both pride and modesty. The conscious-
 ness of      my defects has         been   weighing     upon me.         It has sna-

 tched        away my peace of mind,             and has left me greatly
 disturbed for the          last few years.


          Fortunately, about 2 or 3 weeks ago, Guruvaryva Rambhiu
 Ranade came to           see     me, during   his recent       stay at    Belgaum.
We had no prior direct contact with each other. Even though |
knew full well about his great scholarship, his pure character,
his spiritual experiences.            | had no direct contact with him.
When [ came 10 know that he was coming                    to Belguum. | wrote
to     him    a letter. requesting him to        spare some         time for me
during his numerous engagements here, so that | might find
some solace thereby.              !mmediately | gota      reply of        assurance
from him and accordingly, he did come to see                     me. During our
talk, he informed me that he would soon be going to Sangli
when | told him that I wish to see him again at Miraj at that
time.     [ was,    thereafter, extremely eagar to see him at Mira/.
Hence        | requested the       Rujasiheb of Miruj 10 intimate             tome
the date of his         arrival    there. Accordingly,      |   got a telegram
from him as wellasa letter from Guruvarya. 901 could see
him at Miraj, have the pleasure of hearing his spiritual talks
as well as the blessing of his spiritual guidance. All these
events have taken place during the last three weeks. But they
have reduced my disturbance and have been gradually granting
me some peace.            | don’t claim        to have      attained        perfect
pace, as yet. But | have got the satisfaction of getting the
path     of    peace.     AMahatmaji used to tellus:              “1      have not
seen God: but I have discovered the path of seeing Him.
That is the source of satisfaction to me.’’ Similarly, | 119५४
