age, the tenderness and yearning of Gangadharrao, is really
remarkable. - unique. Such a softness is rarely to be found in
oldage.   Where this exists, God is not far away.                            +

              Gurudeva Ranade-My Father

                  ( By ~ Smt. Vijaya 7. Apte. )

       Almost 8 new era begins with the advent of Sri Guru-
deva in the field of Indian Philosophy; or we may say that he
is one of the brightest stars   shining in the philosophical fir-
7871611 of the resurgent India of the 20th century. His appear-
ance on the   scene was very    necessary when India was   under-

90176 the bewildering and dazzling changes by the contact
with the Western Development of Science. A perplexed mind
ultimately finds solace only when it is able to see within itself,
with 8 heart full of faith, in the Ultimate Power. Thus the
Pathway to the philosophical and mystical sphere was opened
by such illustrious seers who had shunned the bonds of old
dogmatism. Here | can mention the names of Sri Ramakrishna
Paramahamsa, Swaml Vivekananda, Sri Rabindranath Tagore,
Sri Aurobindo Ghosh, 00. S. Radhakrishnan and Sri Gurudeva
Ranade. Gurudeva Ranade was the builder of the modern spiri-
tual empire. He stands before us as an intellectual and mysti-
calcollossus. As Dr. S Radhakrishnan 59/5- “ He taught not
merely with his intellect but with his whole life. Philosophy

                                327
Rambhau Maharaj



for him was not a profession but a consuming passion. My
life is richer for having known him. ? Even the Philosopher-
 King. like Dr. Radhakrishnan accepts Sri. Gurudeva as the
unparalleled Mystic of the day.

      Recently Dr. Burch from America ( Head of the          Deptt.
of Philosophy,    Massachusetts University ) wrote : ^“    Had not
Providence brought me to this venerable         man, probably the
most spiritually advanced person । shall ever know—to whom
॥ was already bound by ties of mutual     affection in   order that
he should be my spiritual preceptor ? ”


       The world is verily aware of his unique greatness.     Still
 it can know only the outward appearance of such uncomman
 personalities; as Sri Ramdas says,

           गुप्त आहे उदंड वन, काय जाणती सेवक जन ।
                 तयासी आहेते ज्ञान, वाह्यात्काराचे ॥
 Now that we have lost such a precious diamond, the only way
 left to us, is to enlighten ourselves with his writings and his
 teachings.


        Writing unveils the Man. Gurudeva Ranade was a lover
 of deep study of any topic taken on hand—may be of Literature,
 Science, or Philosophy. He used to go to the original sources
 of the matter—nay, even of the ‘ words’ also and that is why
 he could enhance the treasure of the ‘word-kingdom’. He
 coined many new words in the philosophical and mystical
 \iterature. He was a Seer-Scientist of life and an apostle of
 virtues. Moral character isthe basis of all success, A real
 spiritual Jife can only be built on the moral basis. Thus virtues
  meant everything for him: “ Character is the milk of life. ”

        There was no superficiality in his writings.     He was a
  voluminous writer and contributed -original doctrines to the

                                  328
                                                              My father


world of philosonhy: Logical development, consistency, brevity
and    accuracy are the characteristics   of   his   style   making   it
unique.    He used to sum up his ideas ॥ the end so that the
true   lover of knowledge could get a clear picture of the views

Propounded     in   the beginning. His style was lucid.      He   hada
mastery over English as well as over Latin, Greek and         German.

H: was well acquainted with the sainty literature in almost
all Indian Languages and all the more with that in the Alma
Mater Sanskrit. A profound scholar of Sanskrit that he was,
his Magnum opus       ‘‘ The Constructive Survey of     Upanishadic
Philosophy ” gives many new interpretations of           the original
Sanskrit texts.     He used to say that we should study every
problem in the way of the Kantian Critique. All his writings
are    constructions through     critical expositions. His was a
synthesising approach. A spirit of reconciliation runs through
all his literature. For example: we can see the five antinomies
in the Gita reconciled only on a view of Reality which regards
the realisation of God as the be-all and the end-all of all
Existence. He himself says, “ This mystical view of Reality
alone will enable us to reconcile all the intellectual dogmas
that have infested the philosophies of the world. What we
feel and what we realise should alone constitute our philoso-
phy ? And all this can only be achieved by God- Devotion
which is the central thread of all virtues. The Christian and
the Platonic virtues are all shown to be arising from one guid-
ing virtue viz “ भवति , ” so too, the virtues enunciated in the
Gita. Thus Devotion alone would lead to the realisation of
Self which constitutes the foundation and the peak of al
Thought and Existence. The final verdict on the two controver-
sial doctrines in Indian Philosophyi. € ज्ञातात्तरकम 210 ज्ञान-
कर्म- समच्यय is that ज्ञान is not an event but aprocess. Thus
Gurudeva Ranade combined in himself, in quite 4 unique way,
the different roles of Literator, Philosopher and a great Mystic
He was a mystic all his life.


        Simplicity was a significant trait of his personality. He

                                329
Rambhau Maharaj



has an abounding love for all who came in contact with him-
whosoever he may be, a prince or a man on the street. He had
a special affection for the students who stayed with him. His
love for his.disciplesis also   well-known. Everyone who came
near him, thought that he was loved most by Sri Gurudeva.
That was the one and the only one feeling that everybody had
forhim    His serene smile and sanctifying presence, spread
peace, love and good-will everywhere. He appreciated only the
virtues in others without noticing their drawbacks.       He   was a
saint of this type:-



                परगुण-परमाणून्पर्वतीकृत्य नि त्यम्‌
                 नि जहदि   वि कसन्तः सन्ति   सन्त: Praca: i

 This gave an impetus to enhance the goodness in others: This
 is why all his disciples kelieved that their      spiritual   teacher
 loved them most.


         How can 1 be an exception to the rule? Having the
 privilege of being hisonly daughter, | am sure that all the
 goodness and happiness | have achieved in my life are due          to
 the blessings and dignified     love that   have been showered on
  me by His Grace. People may think that amystic who hes
  realised God will not be 2016 to play his role properly as a
  father or as the head of the family just like a worldly man.
  All the saints and the intellectuals of the world, like Tukaram,
  Ramadas,   Mira, Kabir or Socrates, quite justify the above
  statement. But | can say with pride that my father well syn-
  thesised the worldly & the spiritual heights. His wasnct
  mere Renunciation, but his was Renunciation in action. He
  remained in the world but was not of it, as the adage goes,
  पद्मपत्रमि वाम्भसा , My father never forgot his duty and love
  towards us. The only thing was that his ways of expression
  were altogether different from those of a common man. And
  that is why people thought, that he had no family-life at all.

 ards    us   was    just the reverse to what           others     thought

              How I Found My Gurudeva


                  ( By ~ Dr. N. S. Christian )

      A seeker of Truth since my boyhood, with      Religion and
Philosophy, Mvsticism   and Yoga as     my hobby, 1 have been a
friend of sadhus and fukeers. Often | fell a victim of   deception
and fraud; still the orange-clad attraction swayed over me. I
read 8 large number of books and visited 45/८4/7145 in    search of
mystic knowledge.
              | have a profound regard for our Land of
Wisdom, its unbroken chain of saints and sages,      the Ancient
Scriptures and our rich cultural and spiritual heritage.


      During those days I had been practising Kundalini Yoga
without a Guru to guide me,    by just following     instructions
given in books on the subject. One night, during my deep
meditation, | exoerienced a terrible psychic shock, pertaining
to the rising of Kusdalini-Sakti, the details of which are too
long to be recorded here. Since then,      [   had experienced a
strange mental ard bodily distress, ranging from ॐ sense of
fulness and intoxication toa fear of impending death, with
fluctuations in my pulse, arid varied and vague          symptoms,
                                                 How I Found my Gurudeva


probably due to         >    disturbance of my       autonomic nervous
svstem. Sleep had completely disappeared and often । got
into ecstatic states and trances with the development of visual

and auditory signs pertaining to Yoga. My friends, who took
me on a jeep to Ganeshpuri, have been witnessing them during
our journey. We visited Swami Nityananda late in the evening
and    |    implored   him   to bless me. He placed     his hand   on my
head       and exclaimed,     “‘.Accha,   Jav,   Abhi 1711697 Jav ”. We
reached Bombay late at night and rested at the Archaeological
guest rooms situated on the Fort at Sion.            The next morning
was    Asadha-Ekadasi.        |   woke up early    at 4A. M. and was
reciting `" Lalita-Sahasra-Nama’”’. My friends were snoring in
their slumber after the tirescme jeep-drive the previous day, a
distance of 250 miles in torrential rain all along the journey.
On reaching the closing lines which mean, “‘Imperishable
embudiment of compassion, Light in my darkness *' etc. while
reciting the thousand names of The Divine Mother of the
Universe, I fell into a trance and lost myself in ecstacy with a
vision of the Mother. My friends woke up to see me moaning
with a flushed face, my eyes pouring out tears. They were
greatly perturbed until | recovered after nearly half 80 hour-
The whole day | wasina blissful state. Dr. Kulkarni noted
fluctuation in my pulse and he took me to our friend, Dr. Tul-
pule, eminent cardiologist and Professor of Medicine at the
J. J. Medical College, residing at Dadar, himself a great devo-
tee and a pious soul. The learned doctor found nothing abnor-
mal in me. The cardiogram and X-Ray revealed a perfect heart.
| was experiencing a sense of fulness and intoxication and a
feeling that my body would burst out. | requested the Doctor
to prescribe medicine. Dr. Tulpule advised me to see Gurudeva
Ranade of Nimbal and said that there was nothing wrong

                Mysterium Tremendum

                   ( By ˆ Prof. 8. K. Gupta )


        A sketch of a God-realiser by one who is not so. is
hardly adequate. Unless the spiritual depth which Ranade
attained is fathomed, one can hardly depict him appropriately.
Before | attempt a description of Ranade from the standpoint
of anon-realiser of God, | bow down in veneration to the
* Mysterium Tremendum’      that is Ranade.


        | had the privilege of being his disciple for two years
at the University of Allahabad. He taught Indian Philosophy
in M A. (previous ) class. | still remember his explanation of
‘ Tajjalan `° ~ the cryptic word from Chhandogya Upanishad.
That from which all things originate,     into which they are
ultimately resolved and in which they live and have their
being is ° Tajjalan.’ All powers in this universe, physical or
mental, are manifestations of His energy. He is the essence
Of all beings. One who realises Him finds Him in all beings.
As the Gita says. He 8010435 in all multiplicity undivided.


                               345
Rambhau Maharaj



        Sarbabhufesu jenaikam bhavamabyayam iksate
        Abibhaktam bibhaktesu tajjnanam biddi sattvikam

                                       (Chapter 18, verse 20)        शै


      The full import of the term‘ Tajjalan’ only a mystic
can realise. And a mystic can explain it the best. Even though
the listeners are non-mystics and so cannot enter much deep
into its meaning, yet they are impressed. They are aware of
a grand presence. An impression of alife time is created.

        His success as a teacher was manifest all the more at the
level of guiding resaarch. ॥ was a privilege to ba a research
 scholar under his guidance. Original ideas and scholarly
dissertations are specialities. First rate theses and books by
research scholars are the outcome of his guidance. Dr. Chandra
Dhar Sharma, the Author of that excellent book ` ^ Critical
Survey of Indian Pnilosophy, ` was a research scholar under
Ranade’s guidance, when | was a student of M.A. Class. His
book contains scholarly dissertations and views of Ranade.
J happened to meet him, when he came to Orissa as the
President of All Orissa Philosophy Association. He agreed
with me that his book contains Ranade’s views, which add
 much to its excellence. |


       Not only his scholarship but also his unassuming nature
 that made Ranade an attractiv< personality. 1( was a pleasure
 10 meet him at zhis lodge. His affable nature and sparkling
 humour made his company enjoyable. One has the sense of
 something special    about     him.    And yet during my two        years
 stay at Allahabad, | could         never know that he was a God-
 realiser. Several years 81167| pass2Jj out from Allahabad Uni-
 versity, | happened to read his epoch making book “ Pathway

          के    सर्वभूतेषु येनेक भावमव्ययमीक्षत ।
               अवि भक्तं वि भक्तेषु तज्ज्ञानं वि द्धि   सात्वि कम्‌ ॥।

                                                 Mysterium Tremendum



to God in Hindi Literature ’’. | realised then that he was God-
16811587.   A   book   on God   written   by a   God-realiser   has   an
amazing depth      and   a   wonderful charm. The reader realises,
that here is something above the ordinary. Such a book stands
Out from other books on God,       written by non-realisers. There
is a book on contemporary Indian Philosophy, wherein the Philo-
sophies of eminent modern philosophers of India including
Ranade are given, through their own writings. | noticed therein
that Ranade’s essay surpassed all other essays in depth. The
other essays have high philosophical acumen, but not the depth
of Ranade, which is the outcome of God-realisation. All the
books written by Ranade are outstanding. They bear the
stamp of his deep spiritual insight. Tnough he is physically
no more, one can feel the influence of that liberated soul,
through his books. It can lead a person to immortality.

                 Gurudev As | saw him.

                        ( By I P. Singh )


     It was the spring of 1951. A fellow student of Philosophy
Department in Allahabad University informed me that Prof.
R. 0. Ranade was going to give a talk on “ Mysticism in
Hindi Literature '' later in the evening. | had heard a great
deal about Prof. Ranade—as H3ad of tha Department of
Philosophy, as Dean of the Faculty of Arts and as Vice
Chancellor of the University. | also had read some of his
published works. But, | had never met him till that time. Even

                                   (1)
      Between 1952 and 1956 1 wasin the close contact of
Prof. R. 0. Ranade. He used to come to stay at Allahabad
every year from January or February to April and May. During

                                  360
                                                                 क     क   क   क   ककः   — `   व्क




                                           Dr. Ranado's Msgnotic ‘Attraction


his stay | was privileged to meet him               almost every day. So 1
got the opportunity of holding numerous sittings with him.
But in each        sitting   |   found him        in new perspectives.      The
spirit in him was ever new. It was difficult to understand him
completely.    The only gain was,              that| got   a   new   inspiration
to    meet   him     again.      Each     encounter    with his personality
invariably 160 to another. Such was the magnetic attraction
in it !


      Today he is no more in his earthly coil. But still | conti-
nue to see him, or rather remenber him, as [ used to do
during the fifties. Indeed hardly a day passes off when |
do not see him in his meditation pose. His personality is,
undoubtedly, immortal, not only because it is enshrined in
his immortal works, but also because it is living in the
lives of his numerous followers and disciples. | fully subscribe
to the view of the great Hindi saint. Nabhadasa who says
in his Bhuktamala that love for God, the man who has this
love, God and the teacher of the man—these four constitute
one single personality. So wherever there is love for God
initiated by Prot. Ranade or his disciples, there he is living in
the very form his earthly existence signified. The continuity
of his spiritual tradition, message and meditation has made
him immortal in the true sense of the word. Tnose who nave
this sense can see him even now.



                                        (11)


          | have    1191५ exo2zriences about him               and it is not
possible to record allof them here. So [ shall describe only
two or three of tnem and leave tha rest for some future
occas‘ons. Prof. Ranade had attained to the state of dasire-
lessness Tnere was no trace of any desire or longing in him.
He did not suffer even from the last infirmity of human mind,
४12   Love for fame. Wnen Prof. S. Radhakrishnan became the
Vice-President of India,           | asked him to          comment on his


                                    - 361
Rambhao Maharaj



appointment. He   expressed his happiness over it    and said
that it augured well for the good of the nation.    But when
॥ asked him whether he himself wished to be the Vice-
President or President of India, he replied emphatically in
the negative and said, “| have dedicated my life to God-
realization. Is there anything more valuable ? why do you
think of the undesirable ? ”

      These talks with Prof. Ranade have revealed to me
one thing, inter alia, that he was completely committed to
philosophy and religion. Whereas his contemporaries and
colleagues sought the reward of their services to philosophy
and religion and left philosophy for political and social work,
he did not do so, for, he was above the State. He was in the
line of Indian Rishis and saints that were not enamoured of
 State and its power.

       Such was his love for philosophy. | have yet to come
across a teacher of philosophy who is as devoted to philosophy
as Prof Ranade was. In fact he was philosophy incarnate. who-
soever came in his contact became a philosopher in his own
right. To know him was to know philosophy. To know the
philosopher was to be a philosopher. Bruhmu Veda     Brahmaiva
Bhavati.

             A     Renowned Philosopher-Saint

                       ( By : Sri K. P. Kulkarni)


      One of        our    popular      professors    was Shri Rambhau
Ranade. He taught us Carlyle’s ‘ Heroes’. The town Kolhapur
was a common bond that had fostered between us 8 sense of
reciprocal kinship. Shri Bapurao~ Ranade, his step-brother, was
8 teacher to      allof us and        Rambhau made frequent           trips to
Kolhapur to meet him.          Rambhau was also           the   maternal uncle
of Narahari       Damle, one of ourclose circle. At every University
examination, Rambhau used to rank first and make a rich haul
of prizes    and scholarships.         Naturally every one of his visits
to the Damle’s drew us thither in                   curiosity as     well    as
admiration, Of course in             the heart of hearts we were making
mental notes 811 6 while of the ideal scholar’s style of walk
and talk,    his general turn out,          his bearing, his fads and what
not ! Being with him,
                    at least for               a   while, was a matter of
self-gratulation for us.        That    year particularly       Rambhau had
secured     the     much   coveted Chancellors             Gold    Medal    for

Philosophy at        the M. A. examination.               Fergusson College,
therefore, held for       us   the   dual    attraction    of   Or. Gune    and



                                       363
Rambhau Maharaj



Rambhau Ranade, Sharp of intellect, sweet in nature and
unassuming in disposition he always impressed one at first
sight. He was apersonification of good nature. Physically
however he looked somewhat frail But his profound erudition
more than compensated this shortcoming. He used to be
dressed in avery simple style. A clean bright ° dhoti             , a pair
of typical red Poona slippers (जोडा} ,8 loose none-too fashion-
able shirt with thread buttons, a spacious tight collared
shortish coat buttoned up straight, a fairly long muslin
muffler(gqztt) slung casually around the neck, 8 liberal
saffron coloured      paste   mark   on     the    yawning forehead,
a headgear
     ( pugree ) typical of Poona perched at ease and
indifferent on the crest, and baggy dark gown rather shuffling
about in careless defiance of al! order—in such a uniform. if
it could be called one, he used to enter the classroom wa'king
unusually fast. Sometimes he carried a book or two ex‘rain
 his hand while going to the class. The projection of his
personality would easily profess the subject he taught-
 philosophy. From the moment he entered             the   classroom    the
 stream of his eloquence flowed unfaltered till the bell tolled
 signifying     the closure of the hour. The English he      920९6 was
 pitched   low but delivered fast    ard was profound           yet lucid.
 It was packed with meaning cast in classical mould, and
 somewhat ponderous yet within easy grasp of the student. It
 had    about   it the sanctity and majesty of      the Ganges Every-
 time the student felt unmistakably        that,   he had heard some-
 thing     novel   and    extraordinary,     that   he    had    made    a
 successful sojourn into the realm of the unknowable                  and
 that         a charmed moment that
         it was                                had yielded some rare
 acquisition, an experience bordering on the ecstatic. There
 was 8 special Ranade touch about everything of his—unfolcing
 the depth of Carlyle’s thoughts or his superbly fluent elo-
 quence, the uncanny tact of making the student gravitate
 towards him, the magic touch inducing love of literature in the
 student, and the masterly way of re-establishing the ancient
 tie of the teacher and the taught which seemed to mock at the

                                  364
                                        Ronowned philosopher-Saint



heterodox spirit
               of modernity. The       impression        that   he made
on us then stands out in bold relief even now, aftera           lapse of
fortyfive years

The Upanishadic Sage:


        Often    Ranade asked the students to write        essays    and
after going     through them he   returned   them   to    the students
with his own comments,        suggestions and opinions, pointing
out   mistakes therein, if   any. At times he also called           them
home for discussions over the subject matter of the essavs.
He had     two spacious rooms constructed           just beyond 1/3
Fergusson college 1105181; while his family residence was in
Shaniwar Peth. Ranade often spent long studious hours in
these   rooms. We  had nicknamed them as Carlyle Cottage.
Students considered it a rare honour and privilege whenever
they were summoned by Rambhau Ranade for discussions.
By    temperament      Rambhau    was a person       of transparent
candour. With a childlike innocence he used to mix with
Students shaking off typical aloofness, teachers are normally
prone to maintain. This in turn imposed on the studentsa
sense of embarrassment and awkwardness which compelled
them to talk some garbled stuff, sitting under great constraint.
At the cottage he looked 8 veritab'e skeleton of skin and
bones flitting about in his ‘dhoti’ with its back strip
amusingly shaggy and the bulging loops and falls in front
helpiessly dragging along and with his hair-lock a-top the
crown, jumping about in unintentional mischief. Looking
at him one felt one was squatting before some archaic Rshi
for a session of sermons. Rangarao Diwakar ( who later be-
came the Governor of Bihar) was one of his favourite pupils.
Like him many others whose essays earned his appreciation
received invitations to the cottage from him. Once I too had
the   good fortune to receive it.

                        An Ideal Guru.

                   ( By : Surendra Prasad Garg )

       In   1952    1 was introduced to Shri    Gurudev Ranade
Maharaj & went to Nimbal for his blessed darshan.        By   that
time | had not been initiated and was against this tradition of
Guru worship.      When the disciples of Shri      Gurudev recited
verses in praise of Shri Gurudev & prostrated to pay respects
to him, | did not approve of it & a number of doubts about the
qualification of a Guru arose in my mind. It was a most lucky
hour when Shri Gurudev gave a ring and all the disciples and
devotees gathered in the hall and Shri Gurudev delivered his
Pravachan on the qualities of a Guru without my asking this
question to him. He said that a Guru must have the foilowing
qualifications :

       1. He should be himself a self-realised soul having a
deep insight in the Shashtras.
       2.   Secondly area! Guru need not expect any thing from
his disciples. He should look to the welfare of his devotees.
      3. Thirdly, the personal life of a Guru should be abova
board and should accord to the injunctions of the sacred books.


                              - 367
Rambhau Maharaj




He need not indulge in    any practices not recommended by the
Shashtras on the plea that he is omni-pvutent.
       4.    A Guru is omni-scient, all-powerful like God and he
should be bestowing both worldly & spiritual     benefits on his
disciples.


     On hearing this pravachan of Shri Ranade Maharaj, |,
immediately decided to get myself initiated by him. 1 was
lucky to receive initiation next morning.


       In the afternoon, it so happened that the disciples &
devotees were sitting for meditation along with Shri     Gurudev.
By an accident, the thunder struck upon the roof of the hall,
went penetrating to the ground touching the head of one of
the disciples. It was really a very horrible & frightening inci-
dent but none of the persons in meditation was affected. All
kept on sitting silently for the duration of the meditation. At
the end of an hour Shri Ranade Maharaj merely enquired about
the matter     and adviced measures conducting electricity to
earth. He was quite indifferent to the happening.


       The food served to the devotees was quite simple and
Shri  Gurudev used to bless  it by looking at it, before it was
served. He himself was a very abstemious eater & advised that
minimum quality of food should be taken. Otherwise one will
not be able to sit in meditation for a long time.


       At that time    [had been unjustly demoted to the post
of Tehsildar after working as Sub-Divisional Officer & Assis-
tant Secretary to the Government for about tour years. When
1 was about to depart from the Ashram, Shri -Gurucev of his
own accord asked me when! would become an Assistant
 Collector i. €. ऽ. 0. 0. What reply | could give to this question?
 But soon after my return from the Ashram, [ was unexpectedly
 promoted to the post of Assistant Collector. 1( was only due
 to grace of Shri Gurudev. Even today, though I have to face a

                                368
                                                           An Ideal Gurudev



number    of   difficulties   in   life.   now   & then.    But     they    get.
resolved and eventually| find myself in            quite     easy    circum—-
stances, and have no liabilities & worries which generally travel
a worldly person.     It is all due to Shri Gurudev, whois always
al ve   and takes due careof his disciples            & devotees.          | am
quite sure that the grace of Shri Gurudev will grant me love of
God & lead to Bhagwan after this sthool body dissolves.

      During the last 5 days before his departure (Niryan)

          Even after death,        His body remained perfectly lustrous
without any sign of rigor           Mortis or post

                                                    He Lived Paramartha



        The revered Soul passed      away ‘na joyous enjoyment of
* God ’ deeply engrossed in meditation and completely away
from the material world, leaving behind Him, His great immar-
tal works, on realisation of God, with full of           practical experi-
ences. He synthesised both East and West in devotional, spiri-
tual, and mystic aspectsof philosophy, having full faith                        and
reliance on higher Forces.


Gurudeo Dr. Ranade lived ‘Paramarth’ throughout his life. A
Minute observation of the Saint’s life would reveal that the
beginning and culmination of his life was spiritualism-realiza-
tion   of   God   ( Swaroop   - Saksatkar ).            He   used     to       say
“ Spiritualism has been the aim           of my life; let          it be        its
culmination 3150.7 Sri Gurudeo Ranade,              the mystic-saint,
impressed the value of Sabeej Nama and            meditation          on       the
name of God imparted by a God-realised saint,                the     simplest
and yet the most dynamic way of spiritual           realisation          in    the
present world of strife and struggle for existence. By practising
* Sadhana’ for over 50 years, he showed to the present world,
full of distress and miseries,     that    meditation        alone    is       the
easiest and the surest way of attainment of God-realisation and
spiritual happiness. The essential requisites, he             stressed, as
did the great saints of the past and the ancient Seers               of yore
(1१४७), were the cultivation of moral virtues and elimination
of vices and bad qualities, coupled with God-love and God-
devotion and Satsang,     before     spiritual   life    could      be        fully
realised. As aresult
                  of his      dynamic personality, people from
all classes and from all spheres of life, were attracted to him
and revered him as their Spiritual Teacher’-Sadguru.’ Thus this
divine personality blessed hundreds of aspirants with the holy
‘Mantra’ (Name), ever guiding them on the Pathway to God.

            Gurudeva as a Spiritual         Gardener

                    ( By : Sri S. N. Deshpande )


          ‘Nama is a symbol that carries divine power with it
and Its Smarana is a process of constant     identification   with
God ° exclaimed Gurudeva in one of his post-ecstatic monolo-
gues. His one pointed    Divine personality could be perceived
in a cross-section of his whole life as depicted in this   cryptic
but vibrant expression pregnant with his       philosophy of the
Spirit.


          When I was first blessed by Gurudeva with an intimate
interview in June 1934, | was beyond myself with a sense of
exhileration, gratification and sublimation in life. Even befcre
I entered the four walls of his holy abode of meditation at
Nimbal, the repeated thrilling musical exclamations        of the
Divine Name ‘ Narayana Narayana Narayana’ maddened my
soul as these God-intoxicated utterances penetrated my heart
like the sudden flash of a- rumbling column of light from the
 blue. The inexperienced young boy of twenty in me became
extremely impatient and eager to see in person, the unseen

                                374
                                                       Rambhau Maharaj ४



and unknown personality of Gurudeva. 0 my childish fancy -I
had mentally painted         my own picture of Gurudevu as a tall,
stout and an impressive figure lice fnat           of Swami    Vivekanand.
Within a few moments |              was surprisingly disillusioned to
perceive a thin, lean and an emaciated figure of Gurudeva
looking like a mere bony skeleton wrapped with lustrous              silky
skin. The fragrance and the splendour of 215 spiritual self was
ebbing    out fof   his glowing        looks and    his soothing words
which    in   course   of   time,   bathed me in unique compassion,
love, kindness and inspiration never before experienced in my
life. The child 10 me felt that it nas regained its             long lost
mother.


         | was on the threshold of joining the                Agricultural
College for shaping my academic career in             life. Aftera few
words    of   introductory     talk,   Gurudeva     suddenly and     most
unexpectedly referred to my plan of joining the Agricultural
College and endorsed the idea with the following thoughts.
In the words of Curlyle, he advised us to become peasant
saints. To earn the bread for the body we have to take to
agriculture and to cater to the needs and aspirations of the
spirit, we have to cultivate saintliness and reap the harvest
of 116 Divine Hence agriculture and the culture of the spirit
should form the two pillars of evolution of the body and the
soul simultaneously.

       Just as the peasant toils day in and day out to cultivate
his land and add to the fertility of the soil, the saint in man-
has to keep aconstant vigil on the Name of God, day and .
night, and make his encased self worthy of a {light into the `
fathomless ferman.ent of the Divine Cosmos.


       The double personality of a peasant and a saint in man
has to grow side by side, in a homogeneous manner, recipro-
cally complimentary to each other. The human vehicle in flesh-
and blood nas to develop as 8 peasant up 10 certain limit,

                                    375
Rambhau Maharaji



only to outgrow the bonds of human limitations and transfigure
itself into a vehicle of the Divine will. The agriculture has to
sublimate itself into the culture and nurture of the spirit in
man for the evolution of the individual self. This is possible
only through a theo-centric process of surrender of the lowel
Self and an unfoldment of a continuous awareness of the Divine
Name and       Form. Just as the vital process of                breathing goes
on reflexly inspite of our utter neglect and unawareness of the
basic fact that sustains the spirit in this tenament of the flesh,
so also the descending of the Divine Grace and mercy ts conti-
nuous, inspite of human ignorance,               neglect       and_    indifference.
‘The culture of the spirit sets in, when               through        the    blessings
of saints like Gurudeva the individual self catches the                          current
of awareness of the Divine           Name,   and       reciprocally          attempts
to    ascend   the    ladder    of   spiritual    life,   to    mingle with the
descending Grace of the Divine. Then this process of spiritual
awareness becomes as automatic and reflex as the act of
physical breathing.


        For inculcating        in our daily life,       the awareness of this
double process of descent of the divine Grace and ascent of
a devotee, through the method of meditation and dedication,
 we may be benefited by the guide lines suggested by Gurudeva
 Ranade,   as a spiritual Gardener. In                 this context          Gurudeva
compared the growth of a plant with that of the sprouting of a
seed of Divine Name,           in the heart of     a    devotee.       Tne growth
of the seed       and   the seedling depends mainly on three factors.
 The innate potency of the seed to grow, the tirnely plantation
 in a well-cultivated and manured soil,and the opportune water-
ing of the roots and the shoots after eradication of the                         weeds.
 It   is the deepening growth of the unseen roots                      under ground
 that result in      the exhuberance of the foliage above. The huge
 variety of colour, flower, fragrance and                  quality          of   flowers
 and fruits proclaim      tothe world            the    limitless and            unima-
 ginable power of the Divine           Energy.

         The critical    knowledge        and    observation           of    Gurudeva


                                       376
                                             Guruieza as 3 Sp ritual Gurdaner


                                                                    1


as a    botanist      and     plant-pathologis:      could     enab'e   him    to
elucidate the comparison               in    deeper detaiis.
                                                         Meditation on
the name     of God, is        like watering the roots of the plant and
reading    the spiritual literature and            singing     the giory of God
are    similar   to    the    process of sprinkling          the   water on the
foliage    and branches of the plant,              to regulate the process of
transpiration.        If   the roots do not get the timely supply of
water, the       plant      will not        survive and   if   the process    of
transpiration      is not regulated through external sprinkling of
water, the excess evaporation of the water content will weaken
the progress of the plant growth. Thus the relative importance
of both     the meditation and               the singing of        prayers   and
bhajans    is made clear by the gardener in Gurudeva.


         The imposing construction of Gurudeva Mandir with
a huge     garden          round about, on the out-skirts of            Belgaum
reminds me of the fundamentals of                    spritual gardening as
proposed by Gurudevu. An ardent prayer springs up in the
solitude of my humble heart that the Spiritual Gardener may
guide us on the right path        to fulfil tne purpose of गुरुदेव Walt
Gurudeva Mandir.

      Following is the faithful account of an incident that
took place at Sangli, which I described while giving a brief
talk at the Academy of Comparative Philosophy and Religion,
Belgaum, when | visited it last. ©                             N


     | attended a ceremony at Sangli in Ganpati Mandir
when Gurudev Dr. R. D. Ranade and Dr. Radhakrishnan were
present. Dr. Radhakrishnan was then the President of India.
Thereafter, somehow, | was called to the Mal bungalow, a
palace of the Rajesaheb of Sangli, by 91111      Gurudev. | was
specially called to place my views before him regarding Vedant
philosophy, as given by Nischaldas, in his book Vicharsagar.
This was because, ! guess, somebody must have whispered
 into his ear about me. | was a bit surprised at this call. | was
called at 3-00 9. m. in the Mal Bungalow. Accordingly 1 went

15 this a learned man whose manners seem to be quite eccen-

                    Gurudeo as | saw Him
                      By: Prof. 2. M. Upadhye

        It is said that a man gets a new-birth             in spiritual life
after his mere contact    with the Guru            and   this   is what    has
happened in my case in the real sense of the term. It was
the   blessed day, twenty four years ago, when | saw               Gurudeo
for the first time in life.   | was having dark nignt o1           my soul
hankering   after the day-light        and   lo,    atonce,     anew divine
light in the form of Gurudeo flashed forth before me, it was
not the heat but it was the      moon-light soothing my soul by
the presence of the nectar-like rays of the moon in                the form
of Gurudeo. More wonderful thing that | experienced was
that | surrendered myself to Him and his civine touch and
divine laok filled my entire body and | lost myssif for a
minute. | still remember this inexpressible state of my mind
in his presence, He did not say anythiig to me, but every-
thing that | needed to begin Sadhakavastha was conveyed
to me. It was strength to me to leai tne spiritual life                   and
Ihave been trying in my humble way to follow it.

       This is how | saw Gurudeo twenty four years ago.              After

                                 381
Rambhau     Maharaj




my first    visit    to Him,!   was once      again attracted           towards
him and | used to meet him often. In the             meetings        he    spoke
few words, Words of wisdom, full of divine             life    and      it could
electrify any layman near him.           | was such     a fortunate            soul
near him.     He used to explain the source of         vedanta sutras or
a   Rgvedic     hymn on Pisan.       |   could hardly understand                him
because he used to speak indirectly about                 his divine life
through the words therein.           It was beyond my         reach because
1 was far      away from such       life.   [ was a    man of        flesh and
blood.     He was a superman, areal Sadguru            who     inspired         the
Sadhakas      like me for spiritual life and we know that Gurudet
spent his whole life for this mission            and he       lived     for this
Divine mission,         till he breathed his last.


      Whenever | saw Him, 1 alaways noticed divine ligh
around him.| also thought that ॥ was as if meeting Ydajna-
valkya of the Upanisadic            times or ॥ was         meeting             saint
Ekanatha. All the divine qualities were seen in Him and-{ looked
upon him as one such Vibhuti as described in th2 10th chapter
of the Gira.


         He was the embodiment of knowledge and faith to us.
-All the characteristics of an ideal bhakta or a teacher as
‘described in       ancient literature were   also found      in   Him.         Hs
love was grace.his speech was knowledge,his touch was divine,
his sight was nectar-like rays. Tnis was              the feeling         in    my
heart. Wnenever | remember           Him and     his words,[ am                still
thrilled.   Nimbal, the very spiritual seat of his divine life, is a
great solace to many sadhakas like me and! pray                    to     Him to
shower His grace on all the sadhakas to lead the               spiritual life.
 May He take us from darkness to light | May He                take us from
 death to immortality !

                   Gurudev As | Saw Him
                         ( 6. 7. Tulapule )

         It was in the year 1908 that| was first aoquainted with
Gurudev. | had then joined the Deccan College, Poona and he
was
  a Fellow there,      teaching Sanskrit      Poetry to our Class.
॥ lookea upon him then mostly in my capacity          as   one    in-
terested in moral and spiritual Philosophy. But when [ was
initiated by Shri Bhausaheb Maharaj in 1911, | began to
regard him inmy capacity as 8 Sadhak, and began to regard
him as an      ideal Sadhak. My fortunate contact with           him
went on      ripening into a    close   intimacy    right upto his
demise in 1957. During this lung period of nearly fifty years,
] had the unique 9००१ fortune of studying the various facets
of rich, brilliant, pure and purifying personality. | give below
some of my reminiscences of Gurudev’s life and personality :-
    a)    His wonderful confidence and conviction regarding
his thoughts
          as seen in his casual conversation :-
    i)    Inthe year 1914,   I went to see him at      the Deccan

Rambhau Maharaj




College, Pune, He had to go out for a few minutes         and so he
opened Dnaneshwari and asked me (9 71830 it till he returned
The page contained the following verse from the commentary
on 8. ७. 9/2.


              सुखाच्या पाऊटी । येईजे जयाचि ये भेटी ।
              भेटल्या कीर मि ठी । सुखातेही पडे ॥

       The main idea init is that ॐ Sadhak climbs the path
of God-realization by the steps of spiritual bliss and finally
he becomes one with the bliss itself. ॥ brought this to the
notice of Gurudev and asked, *“ Is there a degree of rising
spiritual bliss even in the Sddhak State? ”. He very gently
said “ Yes, Ganpatrao. If it were not so, how would it be
possible toclimb this difficult path of God-realisation ?”
Later on, in dus course 1 read h:s books and was convinced
that spiritual bliss was the Cen:ral principle of the Science
 of God-realisation.


     ii) During his stay at Nimbal, | once asked, ^“ How is one
 to know that his spiritual Sddkana          has reached perfection?”
 In reply to my question Gurudev immediately quoted the
 following verses from Dasabodha -

        “ पापाची खंडना झाली । जन्मयातना चुकली । ऐसी स्वये
 प्रचीति आलो । म्हणजे बरे ।। मुख्य देवासी ओळ खि ळे । मी कोण हें
 जाणलें | आत्मनि वेदन झालें । म्हणजे वरे ।1 हें ब्रम्हाड कोठोति ATS |
 कासयाचे उमारि ले । मुख्य कर्त्या सि   ओछखि लें । म्हणजे वरे it

 In these lines we are told that God is the only Reality,
 the Self and universe are illusory. One must know this by
  personal experience and this experience annihilates all Sin
  and suffering and becomes a mark of perfection of spiritual
 life. Both these doctrines are clearly reflected in Gurudev’s
                                         1        ot              न
  writings.

                                   384
                                                      Gurudeva As    I Saw Him



        iii)    When | was with him-at Allahabad in 1936,I asked
him, “ We read and hear that there are different ways to God-
realisation      such as    Karma, Jnana,          Bhakti    and Dhyana.   Are
there really such       different ways ? OR, is          there only    the one
way, that of Namasmurana, as practised by us?’’. In reply                    to
my question,       Gurudev        lifted    up his hands and bringing them
down    asa      sign   of his conviction (10 carry conviction) he
said,


        ^ There is no other path to attain God - realisation.” He
further explained          that    Nadmasmarana-        and Self-realisation
attained       through it-is the only way of God-Realisation. There
is none other. In       his books, especially the one on Karnatak
mysticism, Gurudev has sung eloquent praises of Namasmarana
making       it absolutely clear that Nama is God ( God in posse ),
that Nama         is the   symbol of         the   Divine carrying    spiritual
energy and that the process of Namasmarana is the process
of identification with God.


        b)     When one considers Gurudev’s devotion,                love and
respect as well as his gratitude towards his Guru, one is re-
minded of Onanadeva’s commentary on आचार्यां पासना in 8. ©.

13-7 in Dnaneshwari.It is said that a devotee attains liberation
by developing       intensely any one emotion about God. When
| asked Gurudev, ‘‘ which particular feeling                    about God or
relationship with Him should one prefer?” he said ‘“‘ The
devotee should regard God as his Guru. This relationship
between the devotee and his God-this intense emotion-is the
best’. Gurudev always looked upon his Guru as God incarnate.
To look upon one’s Guru as God and to regard God as one’s
Guru are practically the two sides of the same coin. [ cannot
help feeling that only on account of his incomparable devotion
to his own Guru he gave this reply to my question.


        c)     Once he mentioned             two very       significant points
regarding the Guru’s function towards his disciple. (i) The

Rembhau        Mahara)   .




mother feeds the foetus in the womb through the anbilical

professor had come to Nimbal and he and                 [   were     talking to

with her milk, the Guru also nourishes his disciple spiritually
with his spiritual power. This is an      actual experience,
Ganpatrao. What greater authority can there be than
experience ? In the past | did not impart Nama or initiate
Sadhaks and so | could not experience this. But, when    I
Started initiating aspirants [ began to experience this. ”’
Towards the end              ot 1920 Gurudev        attained   the    spiritual

the demise of Sree Baba in December1933that Gurudev started
initiating others. This incident 2. 21               reflects his extrem?
humility and modesty.


         d)     Gurudev very rarely spoke       about his      experiences or

would he found significant :—


         Gurudev could easily read the character of aman

       i)      When   । got   my M.A.        degree, | said to           Gurudev in
1914, “° | have to discharge some family                  responsibilities.       If !
get a fairly well-paid job, 1 shall be                ableto discharge these
properly. In 1915 | secured a post of the Superintendent of Post
Offices. । wrote to Gurudev about this good news In his reply
of congratulations he         wrote ” God fulfils 811 our pious wishes—
©   सत्यसकल्पाचा दाता भगवान. ’ In this reply was implied the
gentle warning of keeping one’s desires meritorious.
        ii)    In 1915, when |      wasa          Professor at     Ajmer, there
 was some small growth in my spiritual experience and | wrote
 to him about this. He wrote back, “ Strike the iron while                          it
  is hot ’’.


        iii)     Sometimes he gave me a stern warning, of                      course


                                       388           .;
                                              Gurudeva As I SawHim



out of affection. In a letter or two | had mentioned some gran-
diloquent    thoughts.   He   wrote   in   reply “° Do   not   entertain
morbid ideals which you can never attain. ”’


       iv)   In 1942, when I was Deputy Post Master General at
Lahore, Gurudev wrote to me “| remember you often and inmy
meditations. ” | could not understand his intention, but I can-
not describe the great satisfaction | felt on reading the letter.

        h) Once, while [ was walking with Gurudev, he said
as if to himself, ^“ Maharaj had become one with the universe -
How bitterly Nature must have mourned when Maharaj
passed away ”. | did not grasp the meaning of these words.
But they went deep down intu my heart.
